Personal discipline in purity, modesty, and diet protects the heart from barriers to Allah.

The second set of personal etiquettes focuses on physical purity and moral vigilance. The seeker is instructed to constantly maintain wudu, avoid sleeping in a state of janabah, and observe strict modesty regarding his private parts. He must not covet, continuously hold himself accountable, and eat only lawful food, struggling with doubtful sources. Most critically, he must guard his gaze from beautiful forms (women and youths), as these are barriers that block divine openings.

Primary Etiquettes of Dhikr
Lists three primary etiquettes for the dhikr practitioner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three primary etiquettes that a dhakir should observe before beginning dhikr.

Core Idea
Three simple acts prepare the heart for the journey of dhikr.

This lesson introduces the first set of etiquettes that a person engaged in dhikr (remembrance of Allah) should follow. These are immediate actions to be performed before starting the dhikr, setting the stage for a spiritually fruitful session.

Guided Path
1
Read the primary adab
Read the Arabic passage listing the three etiquettes. Notice the pattern 'وأن...' indicating each is a prescribed action.
The three are: sending salawat, facing qibla, and bringing the shaykh to mind.
2
Understand the significance
Each etiquette has a purpose: connecting to the Prophet, aligning with the best direction, and seeking spiritual companionship.
3
Reflect on the order
The order is intentional: after salawat and qibla, one brings the shaykh to mind then starts dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الذاكر
وأن يصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كذلك.
وأن يستقبل القبلة لأنها أفضل الجهات.
وأن يستحضر شيخه ليكون رفيقه في السير، ثم يشرع في الذكر.
ثانياً: الآداب المصاحبة
فأن يستحضر معناها إجمالاً.
وأن يحقق الهمزة، ويمد ألف (لا) مداً متوسطاً، ويفتح ها (إله)
ويطالع كتب القوم؛ ككتب سيدي عبد الوهاب الشعراني؛ فإنها تعلم الآداب.
وحاصل ما هنالك أن طريق القوم سداها هذه الآداب، ولحمتها: الذكر، فلا يتم نسجها إلا بهما. انتهى.
Etiquettes of the Dhakir: And that he send salutations upon the Prophet ﷺ likewise. And that he face the qibla because it is the best of directions. And that he bring to mind his shaykh to be his companion in the journey, then begin the dhikr. Secondly: The accompanying etiquettes: That he grasp its meaning in summary. And that he realize (correctly pronounce) the hamza, prolong the alif of 'la' with medium prolongation, and open the ha of 'ilah', and study the books of the folk; like the books of Sayyidi Abd al-Wahhab al-Sharani; for they teach the etiquettes. The summary of that is that the path of the folk: its warp is these etiquettes, and its weft is the dhikr; so its weaving is not completed except by both. End.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the etiquettes (adab) specific to the one engaged in dhikr (remembrance of God). It first lists three primary adab: sending blessings upon the Prophet, facing the qibla, and mentally present the shaykh as a companion. Then it presents the 'accompanying etiquettes' which include grasping the meaning of the dhikr formula, pronouncing it correctly (e.g., the hamza in 'Allah', the medium prolongation of 'la', and opening the 'ha' of 'ilah'), and studying the works of the awliya like Abd al-Wahhab al-Sharani. The passage concludes with a metaphor: the path of the spiritual folk is like woven cloth; its warp (the vertical threads) is these etiquettes, and its weft (the horizontal threads) is the dhikr itself—both are necessary for a complete weave.

Key Terms
آداب الذاكر
ذكر
قبلة
شيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the third primary etiquette mentioned in the passage?
A) Send salawat upon the Prophet
B) Face the qibla
C) Bring the shaykh to mind
D) Recite dhikr

Key Takeaway
The three primary etiquettes prepare the dhakir's heart by connecting to the Prophet, the qibla, and the shaykh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are about to begin dhikr. Have you ever paused to send salutations upon the Prophet ﷺ first? If not, what is holding you back from this simple act of connection?
?
Do you truly believe that facing the qibla makes a difference in your worship? Have you ever tested this by intentionally facing it and noting the change in your concentration?
?
Can you honestly say you have a shaykh or spiritual guide that you bring to mind? If not, why haven't you sought one, knowing the Prophet ﷺ and the awliya emphasized companionship on this path?

Five Commentarial Points on Dhikr Adab
Commentary on five adab of dhikr phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed commentary on five specific points regarding the etiquette of dhikr: sending salutations, facing the qibla, pronouncing hamza correctly, the shaykh's role, and the direction of the phrase 'ilah'.

Core Idea
Every detail in dhikr adab has precise spiritual and linguistic significance.

This passage from the commentary provides glosses on five phrases from the preceding discussion on the etiquette of dhikr. The commentator clarifies the application of sending salutations, facing the qibla, pronouncing hamza correctly, the role of the shaykh in repelling shaytan, and the direction of the word 'ilah' during recitation. Understanding these details enhances both our practice and our appreciation for the depth of Islamic ritual.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the full translation to get the overall meaning.
2
Identify the five distinct glosses
Notice that each 'قوله' introduces a separate point from the previous text. List them in your mind.
3
Focus on the linguistic point about hamza
Pay special attention to the rule about 'تحقيق الهمزة' – the commentator explicitly says softening the hamza to a ya is a grammatical error (lahn).
This is a common mistake in recitation.
4
Consider the spiritual role of the shaykh
Reflect on the meaning of 'ولولا أن للشيخ مدخلاً' – the shaykh's presence or mental visualization helps repel shaytan during dhikr.
Context: This likely refers to a line in the main text about seeking the shaykh's aid.
5
Understand the direction of 'ilah'
Note that 'ويرجع بـ إله' means directing the word 'ilah' toward one's chest, indicating internalization.
This phrase also seems to reference a missing portion of the main text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وأن يصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كذلك): أي بما تيسر بأي صيغة كانت.
قوله: (وأن يستقبل القبلة) أي إن كان وحده، وإلا تحلّقوا.
قوله: (وأن يحقق الهمزة): أي الأولى والثانية؛ احترازاً عن تسهيلها بحيث تصير ياء فإنه لحن.
قوله: (ولولا أن للشيخ مدخلاً في السير): أي من حيث إن ملاحظته ترد الشيطان عنه.
قوله: (ويرجع بـ «إله»): أي جهة صدره.
His saying: (And that he send salutations upon the Prophet ﷺ likewise): meaning with what is facilitated, in whatever formula. His saying: (And that he face the qibla): meaning if he is alone, otherwise they form a circle. His saying: (And that he realize the hamza): meaning the first and second; as a precaution against softening them so that they become a ya, for that is a grammatical error (lahn). His saying: (And were it not that the shaykh has an entry into the journey): meaning from the aspect that his observation repels the shaytan from him. His saying: (And he returns with 'ilah'): meaning toward his chest.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of glosses (hashiya) explaining specific phrases from the previous section on adab of dhikr. The commentator clarifies that 'likewise' means using any acceptable formula for salawat. The instruction to face the qibla applies only if alone; in a group they form a circle. The 'realization of the hamza' means pronouncing both hamzas clearly, avoiding softening to a ya' (a common error). The comment about the shaykh having an 'entry' explains that the shaykh's presence (or mental visualization) repels shaytan. Finally, 'returns with 'ilah'' is explained as directing the phrase towards one's chest, indicating a subtle point of spiritual practice.

Key Terms
تحقيق الهمزة
لحن
شيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Softening the hamza in dhikr is acceptable as long as the meaning is clear.
Correction: The commentator states it is a grammatical error (lahn) and must be avoided.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the ruling on softening the hamza into a ya?
A) Permitted
B) Recommended
C) It is a grammatical error (lahn)
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The commentary on dhikr adab stresses precision in both outward actions (like hamza articulation) and inward intentions (like focusing on the shaykh and directing words to the heart).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in dhikr, do you take the time to pronounce each letter correctly, or do you rush through it? What does the commentator's emphasis on avoiding 'lahn' reveal about the importance of precision in your worship? Will you commit to learning proper pronunciation for at least one dhikr phrase this week?
?
The commentator says that focusing on your shaykh repels shaytan. Who is your spiritual guide or inspiration in maintaining your dhikr? Have you ever felt distracted during dhikr, and how might turning your attention to that person help you stay focused? Will you intentionally visualize or remember a teacher or role model the next time you feel your mind wandering?
?
You direct 'ilah' toward your chest—meaning your heart. Is your dhikr merely words on your tongue, or does it penetrate your heart? What would change in your daily life if your dhikr truly reached your inner being? Will you pause before your next dhikr and ask Allah to make it heartfelt?

Preliminary Etiquettes of Dhikr
Al-Sawi lists three preliminary etiquettes of dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three preliminary etiquettes to observe before beginning dhikr: sending blessings on the Prophet, facing the qibla, and bringing the shaykh to mind.

Core Idea
Preliminary etiquettes prepare the heart and body for a focused dhikr.

Before engaging in the remembrance of Allah, certain preparations are recommended to align the heart and body. Imam al-Sawi lists three essential preliminary etiquettes that serve as a foundation for the spiritual journey. Let's explore each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Focus on the three items listed.
Notice the phrase 'then begins the remembrance' — these are pre-dhikr acts.
2
Identify the three etiquettes
List them: 1) sending blessings on the Prophet, 2) facing the qibla, 3) bringing the shaykh to mind.
Each has a specific purpose explained in the commentary.
3
Reflect on their purposes
Consider why each etiquette is beneficial: blessings invoke the Prophet's intercession, qibla unifies direction, shaykh repels the devil.
The shaykh here means a spiritual guide, not necessarily physically present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الذاكر
- وأن يصلي على النَّبيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كذلك.
- وأن يستقبل القبلة لأنَّها أفضل الجهات .
- وأن يستحضر شيخه ليكون رفيقه في السَّير، ثمَّ يشرع في الذكر.
ثانياً : الآداب المصاحبة
وأمَّا الآداب المصاحبة له :
- فأن يستحضر معناها إجمالاً .
- وأن يحقق الهمزة ، ويمدَّ ألف (لا) مدّاً متوسطاً، ويفتح ها (إله)
ويطالع كتب القوم ؛ ككتب سيدي عبد الوهاب الشعراني ؛ فإنَّها تعلم الآداب .
وحاصل ما هنالك أنَّ طريق القوم سداها هذه الآداب، ولحمتها : الذكر، فلا يتمُّ نسجها إلَّا بهما. انتهى.
قوله : (وأن يصلي على النبي الله (كذلك) : أي : بما تيسر بأي صيغة كانت.
وإِلَّا
قوله : (وأن يستقبل القبلة أي إن كان وحده، وإلا تحلّقوا. : :
قوله : (وأن يحقق الهمزة) : أي : الأولى والثانية ؛ احترازاً عن تسهيلها بحيث تصير ياء فإنّه لحن
قوله : ( ولولا أنَّ للشَّيخ مدخلاً في السَّير) : أي : من حيث إنَّ ملاحظته تردُّ الشَّيطان عنه .
قوله : (ويرجع بـ «إله») : أي : جهة صدره.
فتحة خفيفة، ويمدَّ ألف (الله) وألف (إله) مداً طبيعياً، ويأتي بالهاء من (الله) ويقف عليها
- وأن يذكر بهمة وقوَّة .
- وأن يكون ذكره رغبةً في مرضاة الله ومحبته وامتثالاً لأمره، لا لرياء ولا لسمعة، ولا لأمر دنيوي أو أخروي.
- وأن ينفي الأكوان من قلبه؛ لأنَّ ملاحظة شيء منها قاطع عن الله، ولولا أنَّ للشَّيخ مُدْخلاً في السَّير ما سَوَّغوا له ملاحظته في حال البداية .
وأن يجلس كجلوسه في التّشهد، إلا لتعب فيجوز التّربع - وأن يُغمض عينيه؛ لأنَّ له تأثيراً في تنوير القلب.
- وأن يبتدئ بـ(لا) جهة اليمين، ويرجع بـ (إله).
- ويختم بـ (الله) جهة اليسار مشيراً إلى قلبه، فإذا أراد ختم الذكر ختمه بمحمد رسول الله .
ثالثاً : الآداب البعدية
وأمّا الآداب البعديَّة : فإنَّه يسكت ويَسكُن بخشوع؛ فإنَّ للذِّكر واردات ترد على قلب الذاكر، ولا يتمكّن الوارد من القلب إلا بذلك،
قوله : (وجب التَّمهل حتَّى يتم حذفه من الأواخر ؛ لدلالة الأوّل عليه، والأوضح أن يقول : ولا يتمكّن الوارد من القلب إلَّا بذلك، فيجب التّمهل حتّى يتمَّ ويتمكن من القلب، فإذا كان الوارد وارد زهد؛ استوت عنده الدُّنيا . . . إلى آخر ما قال.
Etiquettes of the one who remembers (dhakir):
- And that he pray upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, likewise.
- And that he face the qibla because it is the best of directions.
- And that he bring his shaykh to mind to be his companion in the journey, then begin the remembrance.
Secondly: the accompanying etiquettes:
As for the etiquettes that accompany it:
- That he grasp its meaning in summary.
- And that he realize the hamza, and extend the alif of 'la' (no) with a medium extension, and open the ha of 'ilaha' (god).
And he should study the books of the folk, such as the books of Sayyidi Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, for they teach the etiquettes.
The gist of what is there is that the path of the folk has these etiquettes as its warp, and remembrance as its weft; its weaving is only complete by both. End.
His saying: (And that he pray upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, likewise): i.e., with whatever is easy, in whatever formula.
His saying: (And that he face the qibla): i.e., if he is alone, otherwise they should gather in a circle.
His saying: (And that he realize the hamza): i.e., the first and second; as a precaution against softening it so that it becomes a ya, for that is a solecism.
His saying: (And were it not that the shaykh has a point of entry in the journey): i.e., because observing him repels the devil from him.
His saying: (And he returns with 'ilaha'): i.e., towards his chest.
A light fatha, and he extends the alif of 'Allah' and the alif of 'ilaha' with a natural extension, and he produces the ha of 'Allah' and pauses upon it.
- And that he remember with determination and strength.
- And that his remembrance be out of desire for God’s good pleasure and love and obedience to His command, not out of ostentation or reputation, nor for any worldly or otherworldly matter.
- And that he remove the contingent worlds from his heart, because observing anything of them cuts one off from God, and were it not that the shaykh has a point of entry in the journey, they would not permit him to observe him at the beginning stage.
And that he sit as he sits in the tashahhud, except if tired, then cross-legged is permissible.
- And that he close his eyes, for that has an effect in illuminating the heart.
- And that he begin with 'la' toward the right, and return with 'ilaha'.
- And he concludes with 'Allah' toward the left, pointing to his heart. And when he wishes to conclude the remembrance, he concludes it with 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God'.
Thirdly: the post-remembrance etiquettes:
As for the post-remembrance etiquettes: he is silent and still with humility, for remembrance has incoming states (waridat) that come upon the heart of the one remembering, and the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that.
His saying: (Deliberation is obligatory until its deletion from the ends is complete, because the first indicates it. And clearer is that one says: The incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that, so deliberation is obligatory until it is complete and settles in the heart. If the incoming state is one of asceticism, then worldly things become equal in his sight... to the end of what he said.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the etiquettes of dhikr (remembrance of God) divided into three categories: preliminary etiquettes, accompanying etiquettes, and post-remembrance etiquettes. The author begins with the preliminary etiquettes: the one performing dhikr should first send blessings upon the Prophet (ﷺ) in any easy formula, face the qibla as the best direction, and bring his shaykh (spiritual guide) to mind so that he may be a companion in the spiritual journey before starting the dhikr. Then the accompanying etiquettes are listed: the dhakir should grasp the overall meaning of the dhikr, correctly articulate the hamza in 'la ilaha illa Allah', extend the alif of 'la' moderately, open the ha of 'ilaha', and study the books of the spiritual folk, especially those of Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, for they teach these etiquettes. The author then gives a key metaphor: the path of these folk is like a fabric whose warp is etiquettes and whose weft is dhikr; the weaving is only complete with both. The commentary (qawlahu) explains that sending blessings on the Prophet can be in any formula; facing the qibla applies when alone, otherwise they form a circle; realizing the hamza means pronouncing it clearly to avoid turning it into a ya, which would be a mistake; the shaykh's role is to repel the devil; and 'returning with ilaha' means moving it toward the chest. The text continues by noting that the alif of 'Allah' and 'ilaha' should be given a natural extension, and one should produce the ha of 'Allah' and pause upon it. The dhakir should remember with determination and strength, purely for God's pleasure, not for show or worldly gain. He should remove the contingent worlds from his heart, as observing anything of them cuts one off from God; but the shaykh is permitted at the beginning stage. The sitting posture is like the tashahhud, except if tired, then cross-legged is allowed. Closing the eyes helps illuminate the heart. The movements: begin with 'la' toward the right, return with 'ilaha', and conclude with 'Allah' toward the left, pointing to the heart. If ending the session, conclude with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Finally, the post-remembrance etiquette: after dhikr, one should be silent and still with humility, because the remembrance brings spiritual influxes (waridat) to the heart, which cannot settle without stillness. The commentary elaborates that deliberation is obligatory until the influx settles, giving the example of an influx of asceticism making worldly things equal in one's sight.

Key Terms
آداب الذكر
الشيخ
السير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think facing the qibla is obligatory only in congregation, or that the shaykh must be physically present.
Correction: The text clarifies: facing qibla is recommended when alone, and the shaykh is brought to mind mentally, not necessarily physically.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should the dhakir do before beginning dhikr?
A) Recite the entire Qur'an
B) Send blessings on the Prophet and face the qibla and bring his shaykh to mind
C) Fast for three days
D) Give charity

Key Takeaway
The three preliminary etiquettes — sending blessings, facing qibla, and bringing the shaykh — prepare the heart for a focused remembrance of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you begin your dhikr, do you consciously prepare your heart by facing the qibla and sending blessings, or do you rush into it carelessly? What would change if you took these three steps seriously starting today?
?
Bringing your shaykh to mind is meant to repel the devil. Who or what do you actually bring to mind during your worship? Is it your teacher, your distractions, or your ego? How can you train yourself to remember him?
?
Sending blessings on the Prophet before dhikr positions you in his company. How often do you begin your acts of worship with this greeting, and what does that reveal about your love for him? Will you commit to doing it from now on?

Accompanying Etiquettes of Dhikr
Al-Sawi lists accompanying etiquettes of dhikr with a warp-and-weft metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the numerous etiquettes to observe during dhikr, including internal presence, proper articulation, and physical posture.

Core Idea
Accompanying etiquettes turn dhikr into a woven fabric of inner and outer discipline.

Once the preliminaries are set, the dhakir engages in dhikr with a series of etiquettes that cover intention, pronunciation, and posture. Imam al-Sawi provides a comprehensive list, emphasising that both the internal state and external actions are essential for a complete remembrance. Let's examine these accompanying etiquettes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on accompanying etiquettes
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting the variety of etiquettes from understanding meaning to physical movements.
The passage includes a metaphor: etiquettes are the warp and dhikr is the weft.
2
Categorise the etiquettes
Group them into internal (intention, presence) and external (pronunciation, posture, movements).
The text mentions both types explicitly.
3
Understand the warp-and-weft metaphor
The path of the spiritual folk is woven from etiquettes (warp) and dhikr (weft); both are necessary.
This highlights that dhikr without proper adab is incomplete.

Post-Remembrance Etiquette
Al-Sawi describes the post-dhikr etiquette of silent stillness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the post-dhikr etiquette of silent stillness to allow spiritual influxes (waridat) to settle in the heart.

Core Idea
After dhikr, stillness lets divine influxes settle in the heart.

After completing the dhikr, the work is not over. Imam al-Sawi teaches that one should remain silent and still with humility, because dhikr brings spiritual influxes (waridat) that need time to settle. This final etiquette is crucial for reaping the full benefit of the remembrance. Let's understand this practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on post-dhikr etiquette
Read the Arabic sentence and translation. Notice the emphasis on silence and stillness.
The word 'waridat' means spiritual influxes that come upon the heart.
2
Understand the reason for stillness
The text explains that the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except through stillness and silence.
Deliberation (tamahhul) is obligatory until the influx settles.
3
Reflect on an example
The commentary gives an example: if the influx is one of asceticism, worldly things become equal in one's sight.
This shows the transformative effect of the influx.

- That he grasp its meaning in summary.
- And that he realize the hamza, and extend the alif of 'la' (no) with a medium extension, and open the ha of 'ilaha' (god).
And he should study the books of the folk, such as the books of Sayyidi Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, for they teach the etiquettes.
The gist of what is there is that the path of the folk has these etiquettes as its warp, and remembrance as its weft; its weaving is only complete by both. End.
His saying: (And that he pray upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, likewise): i.e., with whatever is easy, in whatever formula.
His saying: (And that he face the qibla): i.e., if he is alone, otherwise they should gather in a circle.
His saying: (And that he realize the hamza): i.e., the first and second; as a precaution against softening it so that it becomes a ya, for that is a solecism.
His saying: (And were it not that the shaykh has a point of entry in the journey): i.e., because observing him repels the devil from him.
His saying: (And he returns with 'ilaha'): i.e., towards his chest.
A light fatha, and he extends the alif of 'Allah' and the alif of 'ilaha' with a natural extension, and he produces the ha of 'Allah' and pauses upon it.
- And that he remember with determination and strength.
- And that his remembrance be out of desire for God’s good pleasure and love and obedience to His command, not out of ostentation or reputation, nor for any worldly or otherworldly matter.
- And that he remove the contingent worlds from his heart, because observing anything of them cuts one off from God, and were it not that the shaykh has a point of entry in the journey, they would not permit him to observe him at the beginning stage.
And that he sit as he sits in the tashahhud, except if tired, then cross-legged is permissible.
- And that he close his eyes, for that has an effect in illuminating the heart.
- And that he begin with 'la' toward the right, and return with 'ilaha'.
- And he concludes with 'Allah' toward the left, pointing to his heart. And when he wishes to conclude the remembrance, he concludes it with 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God'.
Thirdly: the post-remembrance etiquettes:
As for the post-remembrance etiquettes: he is silent and still with humility, for remembrance has incoming states (waridat) that come upon the heart of the one remembering, and the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that.
His saying: (Deliberation is obligatory until its deletion from the ends is complete, because the first indicates it. And clearer is that one says: The incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that, so deliberation is obligatory until it is complete and settles in the heart. If the incoming state is one of asceticism, then worldly things become equal in his sight... to the end of what he said.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the etiquettes of dhikr (remembrance of God) divided into three categories: preliminary etiquettes, accompanying etiquettes, and post-remembrance etiquettes. The author begins with the preliminary etiquettes: the one performing dhikr should first send blessings upon the Prophet (ﷺ) in any easy formula, face the qibla as the best direction, and bring his shaykh (spiritual guide) to mind so that he may be a companion in the spiritual journey before starting the dhikr. Then the accompanying etiquettes are listed: the dhakir should grasp the overall meaning of the dhikr, correctly articulate the hamza in 'la ilaha illa Allah', extend the alif of 'la' moderately, open the ha of 'ilaha', and study the books of the spiritual folk, especially those of Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, for they teach these etiquettes. The author then gives a key metaphor: the path of these folk is like a fabric whose warp is etiquettes and whose weft is dhikr; the weaving is only complete with both. The commentary (qawlahu) explains that sending blessings on the Prophet can be in any formula; facing the qibla applies when alone, otherwise they form a circle; realizing the hamza means pronouncing it clearly to avoid turning it into a ya, which would be a mistake; the shaykh's role is to repel the devil; and 'returning with ilaha' means moving it toward the chest. The text continues by noting that the alif of 'Allah' and 'ilaha' should be given a natural extension, and one should produce the ha of 'Allah' and pause upon it. The dhakir should remember with determination and strength, purely for God's pleasure, not for show or worldly gain. He should remove the contingent worlds from his heart, as observing anything of them cuts one off from God; but the shaykh is permitted at the beginning stage. The sitting posture is like the tashahhud, except if tired, then cross-legged is allowed. Closing the eyes helps illuminate the heart. The movements: begin with 'la' toward the right, return with 'ilaha', and conclude with 'Allah' toward the left, pointing to the heart. If ending the session, conclude with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Finally, the post-remembrance etiquette: after dhikr, one should be silent and still with humility, because the remembrance brings spiritual influxes (waridat) to the heart, which cannot settle without stillness. The commentary elaborates that deliberation is obligatory until the influx settles, giving the example of an influx of asceticism making worldly things equal in one's sight.

Key Terms
الآداب البعدية
الوارد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that after finishing dhikr, it is fine to immediately engage in conversation or activities.
Correction: The text instructs to remain silent and still to allow spiritual influxes to settle, showing that the post-dhikr time is sacred.

Checkpoint
What should the dhakir do after completing dhikr according to this passage?
A) Immediately start another worship
B) Be silent and still with humility
C) Recite the Qur'an loudly
D) Share the experience with others

Key Takeaway
After dhikr, silence and stillness allow divine influxes to settle in the heart, yielding spiritual transformation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After you finish your daily dhikr, do you ever sit in complete stillness, or do you immediately move to the next action? What would it cost you to remain silent and still for just one minute afterward?
?
The text says that spiritual influxes cannot settle except through stillness. When you pray or remember Allah, do you truly give the experience time to penetrate your heart, or do you let it slip away in distraction?
?
What worldly attachments might you need to let go of right now to create that inward stillness after dhikr? Will you commit to practicing this stillness tonight?

Etiquettes of Dhikr: Posture, Direction, and Sincerity
Al-Sawi enumerates the etiquettes before and during dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical and spiritual etiquettes prescribed for performing dhikr (remembrance of Allah), including posture, direction, and intention.

Core Idea
Dhikr requires proper posture, direction, and sincere intention.

This lesson introduces the practical etiquettes of dhikr as taught by the Sufi tradition. Before beginning remembrance, one must adopt a state of humility and focus. Al-Sawi outlines the specific postures and directions that facilitate spiritual connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on dhikr etiquettes
Carefully read the Arabic passage that lists the etiquettes for the dhakir (remembrancer). Pay attention to the sequence of instructions.
The passage starts mid-sentence, but the etiquettes are clearly enumerated.
2
Identify the individual etiquettes
List each etiquette mentioned: doing dhikr with vigor, sincerity, negating worldly thoughts, sitting posture, closing eyes, direction of 'la ilaha illallah', and ending with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'.
Each item is a distinct practice with both outer and inner dimensions.
3
Understand the rationale
Note why each etiquette is prescribed: e.g., closing eyes helps illuminate the heart, sitting like tashahhud fosters humility, negating realms prevents distraction from Allah.
The reason is often stated briefly in the text.
4
Reflect on sincerity
Consider the emphasis on performing dhikr out of desire for Allah's pleasure, not for show or worldly gain. This is the inner dimension.
Sincerity is the foundation of all etiquettes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يذكر بهمة وقوَّة . وأن يكون ذكره رغبةً في مرضاة الله ومحبته وامتثالاً لأمره، لا لرياء ولا لسمعة، ولا لأمر دنيوي أو أخروي. وأن ينفي الأكوان من قلبه؛ لأنَّ ملاحظة شيء منها قاطع عن الله، ولولا أنَّ للشَّيخ مُدْخلاً في السَّير ما سَوَّغوا له ملاحظته في حال البداية . وأن يجلس كجلوسه في التّشهد، إلا لتعب فيجوز التّربع - وأن يُغمض عينيه؛ لأنَّ له تأثيراً في تنوير القلب. وأن يبتدئ بـ(لا) جهة اليمين، ويرجع بـ (إله). ويختم بـ (الله) جهة اليسار مشيراً إلى قلبه، فإذا أراد ختم الذكر ختمه بمحمد رسول الله . ثالثاً : الآداب البعدية وأمّا الآداب البعديَّة : فإنَّه يسكت ويَسكُن بخشوع؛ فإنَّ للذِّكر واردات ترد على قلب الذاكر، ولا يتمكّن الوارد من القلب إلا بذلك، قوله : (وجب التَّمهل حتَّى يتم حذفه من الأواخر ؛ لدلالة الأوّل عليه، والأوضح أن يقول : ولا يتمكّن الوارد من القلب إلَّا بذلك، فيجب التّمهل حتّى يتمَّ ويتمكن من القلب، فإذا كان الوارد وارد زهد؛ استوت عنده الدُّنيا . . . إلى آخر ما قال. فإذا كان الوارد وارد زهد وَجَب التّمهل حتَّى يتم ويتمكن من القلب، فتستوي عنده الدُّنيا، أقبلت أم أدبرت، وإذا كان وارد توكُل صار بعد ذلك مفوّضاً أمره إلى ربه في كل شيء، وإذا كان وارد صبر صار بعد ذلك لا ينزعج من تفاقم الأهوال ، وهكذا من الواردات. قال الإمام الغزالي له الله : ( ولهذه السَّكتة آداب : مراقبة الله تعالى، وإجراء معنى الذكر على قلبه، ونفي الخواطر كلها، وجمع حواسه كلها بحيث لا تتحرّك منه شعرة كحال الهرة عند اصطياد الفأرة، وأن يكتم نفسه بقدر الطاقة مراراً، أقلُّها ثلاثة إلى سبعة، حتّى يدور الوارد أركانه، وألا يبادر بشرب الماء عقب الذكر، فإنَّه يُطفئ ما تحصل من أنواره. والمراد بالوارد : الملك الحاضر للذكر ، فإذا ختم الذاكر، أتحفه بتحفة من ربِّه ؛ لأنَّ العارفين قالوا : جليس الملك لا يخلو من تحفة، فكيف بجليس ملك الملوك ؟ ففي الحديث : «أنا جليس من ذكرني» (۱). قوله : (عقب الذَّكر ) أي : أو أثنائه، فعليه أن يصبر بعد الذكر مدة : أقلُّها نحو نصف ساعةٍ فلكيَّة، وكلَّما كثر كان أحسن . قوله : (فإذا داومت . . . إلخ ) : أشار بذلك إلى أنَّ قوله : (ترقى) جواب شرط مقدر، وهو أحد وجهين في الواقع بعد الأمر، والآخر أنَّه مجزوم في جواب الأمر
And that he remembers with vigor and strength. And that his remembrance be out of desire for Allah's pleasure and love and compliance with His command, not for show or reputation, nor for any worldly or otherworldly matter. And that he negate the realms from his heart; because observing anything of them cuts him off from Allah, and were it not that the Shaykh has an entry in the journey, they would not permit him to observe it in the beginning state. And that he sit like his sitting in the tashahhud, except due to fatigue, then cross-legged is permissible. And that he close his eyes; because it has an effect in illuminating the heart. And that he begin with 'la' from the right side, and return with 'ilaha'. And he ends with 'Allah' from the left side pointing to his heart, and if he wants to end the remembrance, he ends it with Muhammad the Messenger of Allah. Third: The post-remembrance etiquettes. As for the post etiquettes: that he be silent and calm with humility; for remembrance has incoming states that come upon the heart of the rememberer, and the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that. His saying: 'It is necessary to pause until it is deleted from the endings; because the first indicates it, and it is clearer to say: the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that, so it is necessary to pause until it completes and settles in the heart. So if the incoming state is the state of zuhd, the world becomes equal to him... to the end of what he said.' So if the incoming state is the state of zuhd, it is necessary to pause until it completes and settles in the heart, so the world becomes equal to him, whether it comes or goes. And if it is an incoming state of tawakkul, after that he entrusts his affairs to his Lord in everything. And if it is an incoming state of sabr, after that he is not disturbed by the enormity of terrors. And so on of the incoming states. Imam al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And for this pause there are etiquettes: watching over Allah Almighty, running the meaning of the remembrance on his heart, negating all thoughts, gathering all his senses so that no hair moves like a cat when catching a mouse, and holding his breath to the extent of energy repeatedly, at least three to seven times, until the incoming state circulates his pillars, and not hastening to drink water after remembrance, for it extinguishes what is obtained of its lights.' And what is meant by 'al-warid': the angel present for the remembrance. So when the rememberer finishes, he presents a gift from his Lord; for the knowers said: the companion of the king is never without a gift, so how about the companion of the King of Kings? In the hadith: 'I am the companion of whoever remembers Me' (1). His saying: 'after the remembrance' i.e., or during it, so he must be patient after remembrance for a period: at least about half an hour according to the astronomical hour, and the more he does, the better. His saying: 'So if you continue... etc.': he indicated by that that his saying: 'you ascend' is the answer to an implied condition, and it is one of two possibilities in reality after the command, and the other is that it is in the jussive case as an answer to the command.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a combination of instructions on the etiquette of dhikr (remembrance of Allah) and an explanation of the spiritual states (waridat) that result from it. The text begins by listing the proper etiquette for the one performing dhikr: he should do it with vigor, sincerity, and humility; he should negate worldly concerns from his heart; he should sit in a position similar to the tashahhud in prayer, unless tired, then cross-legged; he should close his eyes for better concentration; he should start with 'la' from the right and return with 'ilaha', and end with 'Allah' pointing to his heart; and if he wishes to conclude the dhikr, he ends with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Then the author introduces the third category: post-dhikr etiquette. After finishing remembrance, one must be silent and calm, because the dhikr produces spiritual states (waridat) that descend upon the heart, and these states only settle if the person remains still and attentive. The commentator explains that the phrase in the base text 'وجب التمهل حتى يتم حذفه' (it is necessary to pause until it is deleted) is clearer if interpreted as 'it is necessary to pause until the incoming state settles in the heart.' The passage then gives examples of different waridat: if the state is one of zuhd (asceticism), the world becomes equal to the person; if it is tawakkul (reliance on Allah), he entrusts all affairs to Allah; if it is sabr (patience), he is not disturbed by calamities. The discussion then turns to a quotation from Imam al-Ghazali, who outlines the etiquette of the pause after dhikr: monitoring Allah, keeping the meaning of dhikr in the heart, eliminating all thoughts, and gathering the senses so that the body is completely still, like a cat stalking a mouse. He also mentions holding the breath multiple times and avoiding drinking water immediately after dhikr. The term 'al-warid' is defined as the angelic presence that attends the dhikr; when the dhikr is complete, Allah sends a gift to the rememberer. The passage ends with a commentary on the time required after dhikr: at least half an hour, and more is better, and a grammatical note on the word 'ترقى'.

Key Terms
الذكر
الآداب القبلية
التشهد
الإخلاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why should the one performing dhikr close his eyes?
A) To avoid seeing distractions
B) Because it has an effect in illuminating the heart
C) To imitate the Prophet
D) To prevent drowsiness

Key Takeaway
Dhikr is a comprehensive act involving both inner sincerity and outward posture and direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in dhikr, do you consciously sit with the same posture as in prayer, or do you rush through it while distracted? What would it mean for you to intentionally adopt the tashahhud position and close your eyes to focus your heart on Allah alone, as taught in this passage?
?
The source says to negate the realms from your heart because observing them cuts you off from Allah. What is one worldly concern you are currently clinging to during your worship? Will you actively push it away the next time you remember Allah?
?
The dhikr is to be done 'out of desire for Allah's pleasure and love, not for show or reputation.' Think of the last time you performed dhikr: was there any trace of wanting to be seen or heard by others? How can you purify your intention starting today?

Post-Dhikr Stillness and Spiritual States (Waridat)
Al-Sawi explains the need for stillness after dhikr and exemplifies waridat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why stillness after dhikr is necessary and how spiritual states like zuhd, tawakkul, and sabr descend upon the heart.

Core Idea
After dhikr, be still so the spiritual state can settle in the heart.

Having completed the remembrance, the work is not finished. Al-Sawi explains that a period of silent waiting is essential for the spiritual fruits (waridat) to take root. These states transform one's relationship with the world, trust in Allah, and resilience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on post-dhikr etiquettes and waridat
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'ثالثاً: الآداب البعدية' up to 'وهكذا من الواردات'. This covers the necessity of stillness and examples of waridat.
The text repeats the point about zuhd, so read carefully.
2
Understand the necessity of stillness
Note that after dhikr, one must be silent and calm because the warid (incoming spiritual state) only settles when the heart is still.
The phrase 'ولا يتمكن الوارد من القلب إلا بذلك' is key.
3
Identify the three examples of waridat
Al-Sawi gives three examples: zuhd (asceticism), tawakkul (reliance on Allah), and sabr (patience). For each, note the effect on the person.
Each warid transforms the person's relationship with specific hardships.
4
Reflect on the general principle
The principle is that after dhikr, one must pause until the state fully settles. This applies to any warid, not just the three mentioned.
The text ends with 'وهكذا من الواردات' indicating more possibilities.

In the hadith: 'I am the companion of whoever remembers Me' (1). His saying: 'after the remembrance' i.e., or during it, so he must be patient after remembrance for a period: at least about half an hour according to the astronomical hour, and the more he does, the better. His saying: 'So if you continue... etc.': he indicated by that that his saying: 'you ascend' is the answer to an implied condition, and it is one of two possibilities in reality after the command, and the other is that it is in the jussive case as an answer to the command.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a combination of instructions on the etiquette of dhikr (remembrance of Allah) and an explanation of the spiritual states (waridat) that result from it. The text begins by listing the proper etiquette for the one performing dhikr: he should do it with vigor, sincerity, and humility; he should negate worldly concerns from his heart; he should sit in a position similar to the tashahhud in prayer, unless tired, then cross-legged; he should close his eyes for better concentration; he should start with 'la' from the right and return with 'ilaha', and end with 'Allah' pointing to his heart; and if he wishes to conclude the dhikr, he ends with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Then the author introduces the third category: post-dhikr etiquette. After finishing remembrance, one must be silent and calm, because the dhikr produces spiritual states (waridat) that descend upon the heart, and these states only settle if the person remains still and attentive. The commentator explains that the phrase in the base text 'وجب التمهل حتى يتم حذفه' (it is necessary to pause until it is deleted) is clearer if interpreted as 'it is necessary to pause until the incoming state settles in the heart.' The passage then gives examples of different waridat: if the state is one of zuhd (asceticism), the world becomes equal to the person; if it is tawakkul (reliance on Allah), he entrusts all affairs to Allah; if it is sabr (patience), he is not disturbed by calamities. The discussion then turns to a quotation from Imam al-Ghazali, who outlines the etiquette of the pause after dhikr: monitoring Allah, keeping the meaning of dhikr in the heart, eliminating all thoughts, and gathering the senses so that the body is completely still, like a cat stalking a mouse. He also mentions holding the breath multiple times and avoiding drinking water immediately after dhikr. The term 'al-warid' is defined as the angelic presence that attends the dhikr; when the dhikr is complete, Allah sends a gift to the rememberer. The passage ends with a commentary on the time required after dhikr: at least half an hour, and more is better, and a grammatical note on the word 'ترقى'.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The pause after dhikr is optional or just a habit.
Correction: The text explicitly states that the warid cannot settle in the heart except through stillness, making it necessary.

Checkpoint
What happens when the incoming state (warid) is that of tawakkul?
A) The world becomes equal to him

C) He is not disturbed by terrors
D) He becomes wealthy

Key Takeaway
Stillness after dhikr is essential for spiritual states to settle and transform the heart.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After you finish your dhikr or prayer, do you immediately get up and engage in worldly matters, or do you sit in stillness, waiting for any warid to settle? What does your actual practice reveal about your desire for spiritual transformation? Commit to a specific change starting today.
?
Think of a past spiritual experience—a moment of closeness or insight after worship. Did you allow it to settle, or did you rush away? If you had paused, how might that state have changed your actions or attitude? Write down one practical step to ensure you pause after future worship.
?
The text teaches that if the warid is tawakkul, you entrust all affairs to Allah. Is there any area of your life—finances, relationships, future plans—where you still hold back from full tawakkul? Right now, name that area before Allah and consciously surrender it, even if only for a moment.

Imam al-Ghazali's Etiquettes for the Pause After Dhikr
Al-Sawi quotes Imam al-Ghazali on etiquettes of the pause and defines al-warid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the subtle etiquettes of the pause after dhikr as described by Imam al-Ghazali, including breath control, avoiding water, and the meaning of al-warid.

Core Idea
The pause after dhikr has its own art: stillness, breath, and patience.

Imam al-Ghazali's guidance adds depth to the post-dhikr practice. He compares the seeker to a cat stalking a mouse — total stillness and focus. He also warns against quenching the spiritual lights with water immediately after and defines al-warid as the angelic presence attending the dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's etiquettes from the passage
Read the section starting from 'قال الإمام الغزالي' to the end. This includes the detailed list of etiquettes for the pause (sukta).
The passage also includes a definition of al-warid and a hadith.
2
Identify the list of etiquettes
Ghazali mentions: watching over Allah, running the meaning of dhikr in the heart, negating all thoughts, gathering senses like a cat, holding breath repeatedly (3-7 times), not drinking water after.
Each item is a practical step for deepening the spiritual state.
3
Understand the metaphor of the cat
The cat stalking a mouse is totally still and focused. Similarly, the dhakir should be so still that not even a hair moves.
This highlights the level of physical and mental stillness required.
4
Learn the definition of al-warid
The text explicitly says al-warid is the angel present for the remembrance. This reframes the warid as a spiritual visitor.
The hadith 'I am the companion of whoever remembers Me' supports this.
5
Note the recommended duration
The passage ends with the recommendation to be patient after dhikr for at least half an hour, and more is better.
This gives a practical time frame for the pause.

And that he remembers with vigor and strength. And that his remembrance be out of desire for Allah's pleasure and love and compliance with His command, not for show or reputation, nor for any worldly or otherworldly matter. And that he negate the realms from his heart; because observing anything of them cuts him off from Allah, and were it not that the Shaykh has an entry in the journey, they would not permit him to observe it in the beginning state. And that he sit like his sitting in the tashahhud, except due to fatigue, then cross-legged is permissible. And that he close his eyes; because it has an effect in illuminating the heart. And that he begin with 'la' from the right side, and return with 'ilaha'. And he ends with 'Allah' from the left side pointing to his heart, and if he wants to end the remembrance, he ends it with Muhammad the Messenger of Allah. Third: The post-remembrance etiquettes. As for the post etiquettes: that he be silent and calm with humility; for remembrance has incoming states that come upon the heart of the rememberer, and the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that. His saying: 'It is necessary to pause until it is deleted from the endings; because the first indicates it, and it is clearer to say: the incoming state cannot settle in the heart except by that, so it is necessary to pause until it completes and settles in the heart. So if the incoming state is the state of zuhd, the world becomes equal to him... to the end of what he said.' So if the incoming state is the state of zuhd, it is necessary to pause until it completes and settles in the heart, so the world becomes equal to him, whether it comes or goes. And if it is an incoming state of tawakkul, after that he entrusts his affairs to his Lord in everything. And if it is an incoming state of sabr, after that he is not disturbed by the enormity of terrors. And so on of the incoming states. Imam al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And for this pause there are etiquettes: watching over Allah Almighty, running the meaning of the remembrance on his heart, negating all thoughts, gathering all his senses so that no hair moves like a cat when catching a mouse, and holding his breath to the extent of energy repeatedly, at least three to seven times, until the incoming state circulates his pillars, and not hastening to drink water after remembrance, for it extinguishes what is obtained of its lights.' Etiquettes of Dhikr and the Meaning of al-Warid
Al-Sawi explains the etiquettes of dhikr and the concept of al-warid as the angel present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the etiquettes of dhikr, the three types of spiritual states (waridat), and the meaning of al-warid as the angel present.

Core Idea
Dhikr is an encounter with the angel who brings gifts from the King of kings.

Al-Sawi begins by describing how different spiritual states (waridat) manifest in the heart of the one who remembers God. He then quotes Imam al-Ghazali on the subtle etiquettes of the silence that follows dhikr. Finally, he reveals that 'al-warid' is actually an angel, making dhikr a direct companionship with the Divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the three types of waridat
Carefully read the section describing the states of zuhd, tawakkul, and sabr, and note how each transforms the practitioner's heart.
2
Study the etiquettes from al-Ghazali
Read the list of six etiquettes for the silence (sakta) after dhikr. Reflect on the depth of concentration required.
3
Understand the definition of al-warid
The passage clarifies that al-warid is the angel present during dhikr. Connect this to the hadith at the end.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider the spiritual implications: dhikr brings you into the company of God and His angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الذاكر
فإذا كان الوارد وارد زهد وَجَب التّمهل حتّى يتم ويتمكن من القلب، فتستوي عنده الدُّنيا، أقبلت أم أدبرت، وإذا كان وارد توكُل صار بعد ذلك مفوّضاً أمره إلى ربه في كل شيء، وإذا كان وارد صبر صار بعد ذلك لا ينزعج من تفاقم الأهوال ، وهكذا من الواردات.
قال الإمام الغزالي له الله : ( ولهذه السَّكتة آداب : مراقبة الله تعالى، وإجراء معنى الذكر على قلبه، ونفي الخواطر كلها، وجمع حواسه كلها بحيث لا تتحرّك منه شعرة كحال الهرة عند اصطياد الفأرة، وأن يكتم نفسه بقدر الطاقة مراراً، أقلُّها ثلاثة إلى سبعة، حتّى يدور الوارد أركانه، وألا يبادر بشرب الماء عقب الذكر، فإنَّه يُطفئ ما في جميع ما تحصل من أنواره.
والمراد بالوارد : الملك الحاضر للذكر ، فإذا ختم الذاكر، أتحفه بتحفة من ربِّه ; لأنَّ العارفين قالوا : جليس الملك لا يخلو من تحفة، فكيف بجليس ملك الملوك ؟ ففي الحديث : «أنا جليس من ذكرني» (۱).
Etiquettes of the one who remembers. If the incoming state (al-warid) is a state of zuhd (asceticism), then he must take his time until it fully settles and takes root in the heart, so that this world becomes equal to him whether it comes or goes. And if it is a state of tawakkul (reliance), he thereafter entrusts his affair to his Lord in everything. And if it is a state of sabr (patience), he thereafter is not disturbed by the accumulation of terrors. And so on from the incoming states. Imam al-Ghazali (may God [have mercy] on him) said: 'This silence (al-sakta) has etiquettes: watchfulness of God Most High, running the meaning of the remembrance over his heart, banishing all distracting thoughts, gathering all his senses such that not a hair stirs from him like the state of a cat when stalking a mouse, and suppressing his breath as much as possible repeatedly, at least three to seven times until the incoming state permeates his limbs, and not rushing to drink water after the remembrance, for it extinguishes what is obtained of its lights.' And what is meant by al-warid is the angel present for the remembrance. When the one who remembers finishes, [the angel] gifts him a gift from his Lord, because the gnostics said: The companion of the king is not without a gift, so how about the companion of the King of kings? In the hadith: 'I am the companion of whoever remembers Me.'
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the etiquettes of the one who performs dhikr (remembrance of God). It begins by describing three types of spiritual states (waridat) that may descend upon the heart: a state of zuhd (asceticism) which requires patience until the heart becomes indifferent to worldly gains and losses; a state of tawakkul (reliance) which results in complete delegation of all affairs to God; and a state of sabr (patience) which makes one undisturbed by great horrors. Then it quotes Imam al-Ghazali on the etiquettes of the silence (sakta) observed after dhikr. These include: being watchful of God, keeping the meaning of the remembrance in the heart, removing all distracting thoughts, collecting all senses to the point of complete stillness like a cat hunting, suppressing the breath repeatedly to allow the state to permeate, and not drinking water immediately after dhikr because it extinguishes the spiritual lights obtained. Finally, the passage defines 'al-warid' as the angel present during dhikr, who gifts the practitioner a gift from God after completion, citing the hadith 'I am the companion of whoever remembers Me.' This underscores the spiritual reward and intimacy of dhikr.

Key Terms
الوارد
الذكر
السكتة
الملك الحاضر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'al-warid' refers to a feeling or idea that comes to the heart during dhikr.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that al-warid is the angel present for the remembrance, not a mere feeling.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is meant by 'al-warid'?
A) A spiritual state that comes to the heart
B) The angel present for the remembrance
C) The feeling of tranquility after dhikr
D) The light that appears during dhikr

Key Takeaway
The warid is an angel, and dhikr is a direct companionship with God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that an angel is present with you when you make dhikr, and that when you finish, he brings you a gift from your Lord. Does your dhikr reflect that you are in the company of royalty? Or do you rush through it, distracted and careless? What will you change in your next dhikr to honor this presence?
?
Imam al-Ghazali instructs you to suppress your breath up to seven times until the state permeates your limbs, and not to drink water afterward. When was the last time you exerted such discipline in your worship? What is one small step you can take tonight to practice this silence?
?
The passage says that when you receive a state of tawakkul, you entrust all your affairs to God. Look at the biggest worry in your life right now. Have you truly entrusted it to Him, or are you still holding on? After your next dhikr, will you consciously hand that worry over to your Lord?

The Waiting Period and Condition for Ascending
Al-Sawi explains the waiting period, the conditional for ascending, and defines ranks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the waiting period after dhikr, the conditional nature of ascending ranks, and the grammatical explanation for the alif in ‘taraqa’.

Core Idea
Ascending ranks requires persistent dhikr with etiquettes and a patient waiting period.

Al-Sawi continues his commentary on the etiquettes of remembrance (dhikr). He clarifies that after dhikr, a waiting period of at least half an hour is recommended, and more is better. He then explains that ascending ranks depends on persisting in dhikr with proper etiquettes, and discusses a grammatical nuance regarding the verb ‘taraqa’.

Guided Path
1
Read about the waiting period
The passage states that after dhikr, one must wait patiently for at least half an hour (celestial time). The longer, the better.
This waiting period is part of the etiquette.
2
Analyze the conditional statement
The phrase ‘taraqa’ (you ascend) is the answer to an implied condition: if you persist in dhikr with etiquettes, you ascend. There is also a view that it is jussive after a command.
Grammar note: ‘taraqa’ is in the jussive form but retains its alif.
3
Understand the poetic necessity
The alif in ‘taraqa’ is retained due to poetic necessity, citing a line of poetry. Three scholarly explanations are given for this phenomenon.
This is a grammatical aside that shows the depth of analysis.
4
Define the term ‘ranks’
The passage defines ‘ranks’ as good praiseworthy traits with a commendable outcome. This sets up the next lesson on specific ranks.

من الرجز]
إذا العجوز غضبت فطلق
وما قاله الشارح أحد أجوبة ثلاثة عند إثبات الألف المجزوم، الثاني: أنَّها زيدت للإشباع الثَّالث: أن الجازم إنَّما حذف الحركة فقط، لغة وهي بعض العرب .
قوله : ( رتبة الصَّدِّيقيَّة) : أي : غير الأنبياء، وإلا فرتبتهم لا يصل إليها غيرهم .
His saying: (after the remembrance) meaning: or during it. So he must be patient after the remembrance for a period, the minimum of which is about half an hour by the celestial [time], and the more it is, the better. His saying: (For if you persist... etc.) He indicated by that that his saying: (you ascend) is the answer to an implicit conditional, and it is one of two opinions in reality after the command, and the other is that it is in the jussive as the answer to the command. For if you persist in the remembrance with these etiquettes (you ascend) meaning: you rise. And the affirmation of the alif is a necessity on the pattern of 'wa la tarda-ha wa la tamallaqi', [that is] by this remembrance which includes the etiquettes, i.e., because of it you ascend to the highest ranks. The lowest of the ranks is the Islamic rank: blaming the soul for what has issued from it of violations, and the highest of them is the rank of siddiqiyya (truthfulness) which the servant attains after entering the station of ihsan (excellence). His saying: (on the pattern of 'wa la tarda-ha') and it is the second hemistich of a line, and its first hemistich (from rajaz): 'idha al-'ajuz ghadibat fatalliq'. And what the commentator said is one of three answers regarding affirming the alif in the jussive; the second: that it is added for lengthening; the third: that the jussive only deletes the vowel, a dialect of some Arabs. His saying: (rank of siddiqiyya) meaning: other than the prophets, otherwise their rank is not reached by others.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary that continues the discussion of dhikr etiquettes. It first clarifies that the phrase 'after the remembrance' includes 'during it', and advises a waiting period after dhikr of at least half an hour (by celestial or true time), with longer being better. Then it examines the conditional construction: 'For if you persist in dhikr with these etiquettes, you ascend.' The commentator notes that 'you ascend' (taraqa) can be either the answer to an implicit condition (if you persist, you ascend) or a jussive verb as the answer to a command. The alif in 'taraqa' is affirmed out of poetic necessity, citing the line 'wa la tarda-ha wa la tamallaqi'. The passage then defines 'ranks' (rutan) as good, praiseworthy traits with a commendable outcome. It distinguishes the lowest rank, called the Islamic rank, which is self-blame for sins, and the highest rank, the rank of siddiqiyya (truthfulness), which a servant attains after entering the station of ihsan (excellence). A grammatical aside explains three possible reasons for keeping the alif in the jussive: poetic necessity, lengthening, or a dialect that only drops the vowel. Finally, the passage specifies that the rank of siddiqiyya is for non-prophets, as prophets have an unreachable higher rank.

Key Terms
عقب الذكر
ترقى
الرتب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The alif in 'tarqa' might be seen as a grammatical error.
Correction: It is retained due to poetic necessity, as explained by three scholarly opinions.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Persistent dhikr with etiquettes, followed by a patient waiting period, leads to ascending ranks; the retention of the alif in 'tarqa' is explained by poetic necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you finish your daily dhikr, do you immediately get up and move on, or do you sit patiently for a while, expecting something from Allah? What would change if you truly believed that the waiting period is a condition for ascending?
?
The lowest rank is blaming your own soul for sins. When was the last time you honestly blamed yourself for a sin instead of justifying it? Are you willing to live in that uncomfortable truth to rise higher?
?
You say you want to reach the highest rank (siddiqiyya), but are you prepared to persist in dhikr with etiquettes every single day without fail? What one change will you make today to start that persistence?

The Lowest and Highest Ranks
Al-Sawi defines the lowest and highest spiritual ranks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of the Islamic rank (lowest) and the rank of siddiqiyya (highest), and why the latter is restricted to non-prophets.

Core Idea
The lowest rank is blaming the soul for sins; the highest is siddiqiyya, attained after ihsan, but not for prophets.

In this passage, Al-Sawi clarifies the specific ranks introduced in the previous lesson. The lowest rank, called the Islamic rank, involves self-reproach for sins. The highest rank is the rank of siddiqiyya (truthfulness), which a servant attains after entering the station of ihsan (excellence). Importantly, this highest rank is for non-prophets only, as prophets have an even higher rank.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lowest rank
The lowest rank is the Islamic rank, which is blaming the soul for sins.
This is a form of self-accountability.
2
Identify the highest rank
The highest rank is siddiqiyya, attained after entering the station of ihsan.
Ihsan is the level of excellence in worship.
3
Note the exception for prophets
The rank of siddiqiyya is for non-prophets; prophets have an even higher rank.
This prevents overestimating siddiqiyya.
4
Reflect on the nature of these ranks
These ranks are defined by their characteristics: self-blame vs. truthfulness. They are part of the spiritual journey.

The Path of Dhikr and Ascension through Islamic Ranks
Sawi describes the effect of dhikr and the Islamic ranks from self-blame to siddeeqiyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that persistent dhikr with proper etiquette leads to ascending through Islamic ranks, from self-blame to the highest rank of siddeeqiyyah.

Core Idea
The path of dhikr elevates the soul from self-reproach to the rank of truthfulness.

In this passage, Sawi outlines the transformative power of dhikr. He explains that when performed with proper etiquettes, remembrance of God elevates the soul through various stations, from the lowest of Islamic ranks—self-blame for shortcomings—to the pinnacle: the rank of siddeeqiyyah, or truthfulness. This lesson establishes the foundational understanding that spiritual ascent requires disciplined practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about dhikr and ranks
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice how Sawi describes the effect of dhikr.
The poetic meter note is a grammatical aside; focus on the main content.
2
Identify the lowest and highest ranks
Find the sentence that lists the lowest and highest Islamic ranks. The lowest is self-blame, the highest is siddeeqiyyah.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'rutab'
Sawi defines 'rutab' as praiseworthy natures. Consider what it means for a rank to be a good nature with a commendable end.
4
Connect dhikr to Ihsan
Note that siddeeqiyyah is attained after entering the station of Ihsan. This links the practice of dhikr to the inner reality of worship.

فإن داومت على الذكر بهذه الآداب (ترقى) أي: تصعد، وإثباتُ الألف ضرورة على حد ولا ترضاها ولا تملّقي، بهذا الذكر) : المشتمل على الآداب، أي بسببه أعلى الرتب) جمع رتبة، وهي: الخَليقةُ الحَسَنة المحمودة عاقبتها . وأدنى الرُّتَب الإسلاميَّة لَوْمُ النَّفس على ما صدر منها من المخالفات وأعلاها رتبة الصِّدِّيقيَّة ينالها العبد بعد دخوله في مقام الإحسان، قوله : ( على حد : ولا ترضاها وهو عجز بيت، وصدره: إذا العجوز غضبت فطلق . وما قاله الشارح أحد أجوبة ثلاثة عند إثبات الألف المجزوم، الثاني: أنَّها زيدت للإشباع الثَّالث: أن الجازم إنَّما حذف الحركة فقط، لغة وهي بعض العرب . قوله : ( رتبة الصَّدِّيقيَّة) : أي : غير الأنبياء، وإلا فرتبتهم لا يصل إليها غيرهم . آداب الذاكر وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه ورتبةُ الصِّدِّيقيَّة في نفسها مراتب متفاوتة، بعضها أعلى من بعض، وأعلاها رتبة أبي بكر الصديق له، ولا يعلو مقامَ الصِّدِّيقيَّة إلا مقامُ النُّبوَّة ، فصاحب مقام الصِّدِّيقيَّة لو تخطّى مقامَهُ لنزل في مقام النُّبوَّةِ، إلَّا أنَّ النُّبوَّة قد ختمت بنبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، والصِّدِّيقيَّة لم تُختم فمقامُ الصِّدِّيقيَّة مقام الولاية الكبرى والخلافة العظمى، وهذا المقام تترادف فيه الفتوحات، وتعظم التَّجلّيات، وتتم الله قوله : (وهو أن تعبد الله . . . إلخ ) : أشار للحديث الوارد عن رسول الله جواباً لجبريل ، حيث سأله عن الإحسان، فقال: «الإحسان أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك»(۱)، فأشار بقوله: «كأنَّك تراه إلى مقام المشاهدة وهي شهود الله بالقلب بلا كيف ولا انحصار، كأنه ناظر إليه ومشاهد له ببصره، وشبهه برؤية البصر؛ لأنَّه في الحس والعادة أقوى، وأشار بقوله : «فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك» إلى مقام المراقبة، وهي كما يأتي ملاحظة الحقِّ تعالى في كلِّ حالٍ؛ أي: أنَّه يسمعه ويراه. قوله : (وأعلاها رتبة أبي بكر الصِّدِّيق :أي: ولم يرتق إليها غيره من باقي الأمَّة المحمَّديَّة، فضلاً عن سائر الأمم ؛ لما في الحديث الشريف: ما طلعت الشَّمسُ على أحدٍ بعد النَّبيِّين أفضل من أبي بكر (۲)، وفي رواية أيضاً: «لو وزن إيمان أبي بكرٍ بإيمان الأمَّة «الرجح
If you persist in remembrance with these etiquettes, you will ascend—i.e., rise, and the alif is established necessarily in the meter of 'nor be pleased with them' and 'nor flatter.' By this remembrance—which includes the etiquettes—i.e., because of it, the highest ranks (are attained). 'Rutab' is plural of 'rutbah,' which is a good, praiseworthy nature whose end is commendable. And the lowest of the Islamic ranks is self-blame for what has occurred from him of violations, and the highest of them is the rank of siddeeqiyyah, which the servant attains after entering the station of Ihsan. His saying: 'On the meter: nor be pleased with them'—it is the second hemistich of a verse, and its first hemistich is: 'When the old woman becomes angry, divorce.' And what the commentator said is one of three answers regarding the establishment of the alif that is in the jussive case. The second is that it was added for extension. The third is that the jussive particle only deletes the vowel, as a language (usage) of some Arabs. His saying: 'the rank of siddeeqiyyah'—i.e., other than the prophets, otherwise their rank is not attained by others. Etiquette of the rememberer: It is that you worship God as if you see Him. And the rank of siddeeqiyyah in itself has varied degrees, some higher than others, and the highest of them is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddeeq, may God be pleased with him. And nothing surpasses the station of siddeeqiyyah except the station of prophethood. So the possessor of the station of siddeeqiyyah, if he were to transcend his station, he would descend into the station of prophethood—except that prophethood has been sealed with our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, while siddeeqiyyah has not been sealed. So the station of siddeeqiyyah is the station of the great vicegerency and the supreme caliphate. In this station, openings follow one another, manifestations become great, and God completes... His saying: 'It is that you worship God... etc.' He pointed to the hadith transmitted from the Messenger of God in response to Gabriel, when he asked about Ihsan. He said: 'Ihsan is that you worship God as if you see Him, and if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you.' So by his saying 'as if you see Him,' he pointed to the station of mushahadah (witnessing), which is witnessing God with the heart without how or limitation, as if he is looking at Him and witnessing Him with his sight, and he compared it to sight of the eye because it is stronger in sense and habit. And by his saying 'if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you,' he pointed to the station of muraqabah (vigilance), which is, as will come, observing the Truth, exalted, in every state; i.e., that He hears him and sees him. His saying: 'and the highest of them is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddeeq'—i.e., none other than him has risen to it from the rest of the Muhammadan community, let alone other communities; because of the noble hadith: 'The sun has not risen upon anyone after the prophets better than Abu Bakr,' and in another narration: 'If the faith of Abu Bakr were weighed against the faith of the community, it would outweigh.'
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanatory commentary by Sawi on the path of dhikr and the stations of Ihsan. It begins by stating that if one persists in dhikr with the proper etiquettes, they will ascend to the highest ranks. The lowest Islamic rank is self-blame for faults, and the highest is siddeeqiyyah, attained after entering the station of Ihsan. Sawi then interjects a note on a poetic line, explaining the grammatical rules for the alif in a jussive context, and clarifies that siddeeqiyyah is for non-prophets. Next, he defines the etiquette of the rememberer as worshiping God as if seeing Him, citing the famous hadith of Jibril. He elaborates that the rank of siddeeqiyyah itself has degrees, with Abu Bakr as the highest. No station surpasses siddeeqiyyah except prophethood, but since prophethood is sealed, siddeeqiyyah remains the highest attainable. He interprets the hadith into two stations: mushahadah (witnessing God with the heart) and muraqabah (vigilance that God sees one). Finally, he emphasizes the superiority of Abu Bakr, citing hadiths that he is the best after the prophets and that his faith outweighs that of the entire community.

dhikr
rutab
siddeeqiyyah

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ihsan

Key Takeaway

?

The Two Stations of Ihsan: Mushahadah and Muraqabah
Sawi explains the two stations of Ihsan from the hadith of Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two stations of Ihsan—mushahadah (witnessing) and muraqabah (vigilance)—as derived from the hadith of Jibril.

Core Idea
Ihsan has two stations: witnessing God and being aware that He sees you.

In this passage, Sawi interprets the famous hadith of Jibril, dividing Ihsan into two inner stations. The first is mushahadah, where one worships as if seeing God with the heart. The second is muraqabah, the constant awareness that God is watching. This lesson clarifies that Ihsan is not only about external actions but also about internal states of presence and vigilance.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its interpretation
Read the Arabic passage containing the hadith and Sawi's commentary. Notice how he extracts two stations.
The hadith is from the famous Jibril tradition.
2
Understand the distinction between mushahadah and muraqabah
Sawi defines mushahadah as witnessing God with the heart, and muraqabah as the awareness that God sees you. Compare the two.
3
Reflect on how these stations relate to worship
Consider how worshiping 'as if you see Him' differs from worshiping with the knowledge that 'He sees you'. Both are forms of Ihsan.
