فإن داومت على الذكر بهذه الآداب (ترقى) أي: تصعد، وإثباتُ الألف ضرورة على حد ولا ترضاها ولا تملّقي، بهذا الذكر) : المشتمل على الآداب، أي بسببه أعلى الرتب) جمع رتبة، وهي: الخَليقةُ الحَسَنة المحمودة عاقبتها . وأدنى الرُّتَب الإسلاميَّة لَوْمُ النَّفس على ما صدر منها من المخالفات وأعلاها رتبة الصِّدِّيقيَّة ينالها العبد بعد دخوله في مقام الإحسان، قوله : ( على حد : ولا ترضاها وهو عجز بيت، وصدره: إذا العجوز غضبت فطلق . وما قاله الشارح أحد أجوبة ثلاثة عند إثبات الألف المجزوم، الثاني: أنَّها زيدت للإشباع الثَّالث: أن الجازم إنَّما حذف الحركة فقط، لغة وهي بعض العرب . قوله : ( رتبة الصَّدِّيقيَّة) : أي : غير الأنبياء، وإلا فرتبتهم لا يصل إليها غيرهم . آداب الذاكر وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه ورتبةُ الصِّدِّيقيَّة في نفسها مراتب متفاوتة، بعضها أعلى من بعض، وأعلاها رتبة أبي بكر الصديق له، ولا يعلو مقامَ الصِّدِّيقيَّة إلا مقامُ النُّبوَّة ، فصاحب مقام الصِّدِّيقيَّة لو تخطّى مقامَهُ لنزل في مقام النُّبوَّةِ، إلَّا أنَّ النُّبوَّة قد ختمت بنبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، والصِّدِّيقيَّة لم تُختم فمقامُ الصِّدِّيقيَّة مقام الولاية الكبرى والخلافة العظمى، وهذا المقام تترادف فيه الفتوحات، وتعظم التَّجلّيات، وتتم الله قوله : (وهو أن تعبد الله . . . إلخ ) : أشار للحديث الوارد عن رسول الله جواباً لجبريل ، حيث سأله عن الإحسان، فقال: «الإحسان أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك»(۱)، فأشار بقوله: «كأنَّك تراه إلى مقام المشاهدة وهي شهود الله بالقلب بلا كيف ولا انحصار، كأنه ناظر إليه ومشاهد له ببصره، وشبهه برؤية البصر؛ لأنَّه في الحس والعادة أقوى، وأشار بقوله : «فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك» إلى مقام المراقبة، وهي كما يأتي ملاحظة الحقِّ تعالى في كلِّ حالٍ؛ أي: أنَّه يسمعه ويراه. قوله : (وأعلاها رتبة أبي بكر الصِّدِّيق :أي: ولم يرتق إليها غيره من باقي الأمَّة المحمَّديَّة، فضلاً عن سائر الأمم ؛ لما في الحديث الشريف: ما طلعت الشَّمسُ على أحدٍ بعد النَّبيِّين أفضل من أبي بكر (۲)، وفي رواية أيضاً: «لو وزن إيمان أبي بكرٍ بإيمان الأمَّة «الرجح
If you persist in remembrance with these etiquettes, you will ascend—i.e., rise, and the alif is established necessarily in the meter of 'nor be pleased with them' and 'nor flatter.' By this remembrance—which includes the etiquettes—i.e., because of it, the highest ranks (are attained). 'Rutab' is plural of 'rutbah,' which is a good, praiseworthy nature whose end is commendable. And the lowest of the Islamic ranks is self-blame for what has occurred from him of violations, and the highest of them is the rank of siddeeqiyyah, which the servant attains after entering the station of Ihsan. His saying: 'On the meter: nor be pleased with them'—it is the second hemistich of a verse, and its first hemistich is: 'When the old woman becomes angry, divorce.' And what the commentator said is one of three answers regarding the establishment of the alif that is in the jussive case. The second is that it was added for extension. The third is that the jussive particle only deletes the vowel, as a language (usage) of some Arabs. His saying: 'the rank of siddeeqiyyah'—i.e., other than the prophets, otherwise their rank is not attained by others. Etiquette of the rememberer: It is that you worship God as if you see Him. And the rank of siddeeqiyyah in itself has varied degrees, some higher than others, and the highest of them is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddeeq, may God be pleased with him. And nothing surpasses the station of siddeeqiyyah except the station of prophethood. So the possessor of the station of siddeeqiyyah, if he were to transcend his station, he would descend into the station of prophethood—except that prophethood has been sealed with our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, while siddeeqiyyah has not been sealed. So the station of siddeeqiyyah is the station of the great vicegerency and the supreme caliphate. In this station, openings follow one another, manifestations become great, and God completes... His saying: 'It is that you worship God... etc.' He pointed to the hadith transmitted from the Messenger of God in response to Gabriel, when he asked about Ihsan. He said: 'Ihsan is that you worship God as if you see Him, and if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you.' So by his saying 'as if you see Him,' he pointed to the station of mushahadah (witnessing), which is witnessing God with the heart without how or limitation, as if he is looking at Him and witnessing Him with his sight, and he compared it to sight of the eye because it is stronger in sense and habit. And by his saying 'if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you,' he pointed to the station of muraqabah (vigilance), which is, as will come, observing the Truth, exalted, in every state; i.e., that He hears him and sees him. His saying: 'and the highest of them is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddeeq'—i.e., none other than him has risen to it from the rest of the Muhammadan community, let alone other communities; because of the noble hadith: 'The sun has not risen upon anyone after the prophets better than Abu Bakr,' and in another narration: 'If the faith of Abu Bakr were weighed against the faith of the community, it would outweigh.'
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanatory commentary by Sawi on the path of dhikr and the stations of Ihsan. It begins by stating that if one persists in dhikr with the proper etiquettes, they will ascend to the highest ranks. The lowest Islamic rank is self-blame for faults, and the highest is siddeeqiyyah, attained after entering the station of Ihsan. Sawi then interjects a note on a poetic line, explaining the grammatical rules for the alif in a jussive context, and clarifies that siddeeqiyyah is for non-prophets. Next, he defines the etiquette of the rememberer as worshiping God as if seeing Him, citing the famous hadith of Jibril. He elaborates that the rank of siddeeqiyyah itself has degrees, with Abu Bakr as the highest. No station surpasses siddeeqiyyah except prophethood, but since prophethood is sealed, siddeeqiyyah remains the highest attainable. He interprets the hadith into two stations: mushahadah (witnessing God with the heart) and muraqabah (vigilance that God sees one). Finally, he emphasizes the superiority of Abu Bakr, citing hadiths that he is the best after the prophets and that his faith outweighs that of the entire community.

Key Terms
Ihsan
mushahadah
muraqabah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ihsan is only about performing acts correctly, not about inner states.
Correction: The hadith shows Ihsan involves inner states of witnessing and vigilance, not just outward actions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the station of muraqabah?
A) Seeing God with the heart
B) Knowing that God sees you
C) Speaking with God
D) Asceticism

Key Takeaway
Ihsan consists of two inner stations: witnessing God and being vigilant of His awareness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray or do a good deed, do you genuinely feel as if you are in God's presence? What are the distractions that pull you away from that awareness? Tomorrow, pick one prayer and focus entirely on 'seeing' God with your heart – what changes?
?
You know that God sees you at all times. Is there an area of your life where you act as if He does not? Commit to changing one hidden habit this week because of His constant watch.
?
The Prophet ﷺ described Ihsan as two stations – yet many of us live only in the second, knowing God sees us, but rarely striving for the first. Why do you settle for less? What would it cost you to truly worship as if you see Him?

The Rank of Siddeeqiyyah and the Superiority of Abu Bakr
Sawi discusses the rank of siddeeqiyyah and Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the rank of siddeeqiyyah is the highest station after prophethood, with Abu Bakr as its pinnacle.

Core Idea
Siddeeqiyyah is the highest attainable rank after prophethood, and Abu Bakr is its greatest exemplar.

In this passage, Sawi explains that the rank of siddeeqiyyah is exclusive to non-prophets and has degrees, with Abu Bakr at the summit. He emphasizes that no station surpasses it except prophethood, which is sealed. This lesson highlights the lofty status of siddeeqiyyah and the unique excellence of Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on siddeeqiyyah's definition
Read the Arabic passage that defines siddeeqiyyah and its relation to prophethood.
2
Understand that it has varying degrees
Sawi states that siddeeqiyyah has degrees, with Abu Bakr at the highest. Note that it is not a single rank.
3
Note the relationship to prophethood
Only prophethood surpasses siddeeqiyyah, but it is sealed. Siddeeqiyyah remains open.
4
Reflect on the hadith about Abu Bakr's faith
The hadith emphasizes Abu Bakr's superiority: his faith outweighs that of the whole community.

The Two Stations of Ihsan: Mushahada and Muraqaba
Al-Sawi explains the hadith of Ihsan and defines the stations of witnessing and vigilance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic definition of Ihsan and the two spiritual stations of Mushahada (witnessing) and Muraqaba (vigilance) as explained by Al-Sawi.

Core Idea
Ihsan is to worship Allah as if you see Him, or at least know He sees you.

In this passage, Al-Sawi unpacks the famous hadith of Jibril on Ihsan. He shows that the Prophet's words contain two profound spiritual stations: witnessing Allah with the heart, and constant vigilance of His awareness. Let's explore how these stations guide spiritual excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and explanation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Al-Sawi connects the text to the hadith of Jibril.
The hadith is a central text on Ihsan.
2
Identify the two stations
Find where Al-Sawi mentions mushahada and muraqaba. Understand their definitions.
3
Contrast the stations
Note the difference between witnessing with the heart (mushahada) and vigilance (muraqaba). Why is one considered higher?
Mushahada is described as stronger, likened to physical sight.
4
Reflect on application
Consider how these stations apply to your own worship. How can you cultivate a sense of being seen by Allah?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وهو أن تعبد الله . . . إلخ ) : أشار للحديث الوارد عن رسول الله جواباً لجبريل ، حيث سأله عن الإحسان، فقال: «الإحسان أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك»، فأشار بقوله: «كأنَّك تراه إلى مقام المشاهدة وهي شهود الله بالقلب بلا كيف ولا انحصار، كأنه ناظر إليه ومشاهد له ببصره، وشبهه برؤية البصر؛ لأنَّه في الحس والعادة أقوى، وأشار بقوله : «فإن لم تكن تراه فإنَّه يراك» إلى مقام المراقبة، وهي كما يأتي ملاحظة الحقِّ تعالى في كلِّ حالٍ؛ أي: أنَّه يسمعه ويراه.
He said: (And it is that you worship Allah as if you see Him... etc.): He pointed to the hadith reported from the Messenger of Allah as an answer to Jibril, when he asked him about ihsan, so he said: 'Ihsan is that you worship Allah as if you see Him, for if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you.' So he indicated by his saying 'as if you see Him' to the station of mushahada (witnessing), which is witnessing Allah with the heart without modality or limitation, as if he is looking at Him and witnessing Him with his sight, and he likened it to vision of the eye because it is stronger in sense and habit. And he indicated by his saying 'for if you do not see Him, indeed He sees you' to the station of muraqaba (vigilance), which is, as will come, observing the Truth, exalted, in every state; meaning that He hears him and sees him.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه' from the main text. The commentator, Al-Sawi, explains that this refers to the well-known hadith of Jibril on ihsan. He then unpacks the hadith by identifying two spiritual stations embedded in it. The first part 'كأنك تراه' (as if you see Him) refers to the station of mushahada (witnessing), which is a heart-based vision of Allah without modality or limitation, compared to physical sight. The second part 'فإن لم تكن تراه فإنه يراك' (if you do not see Him, He sees you) refers to the station of muraqaba (vigilance), which is constant awareness that Allah is observing all states. The commentator emphasizes that these are not literal physical sights but spiritual realities.

Key Terms
إحسان
مشاهدة
مراقبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that mushahada is literal physical sight of Allah.
Correction: Al-Sawi explicitly states it is 'witnessing Allah with the heart, without modality or limitation', not physical vision.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Sawi, what are the two stations indicated in the hadith of Ihsan?
A) Mushahada and Muraqaba
B) Tawhid and Ma'rifa
C) Khushu' and Khudu'
D) Sabr and Shukr

Key Takeaway
Ihsan involves worshipping Allah with the spiritual awareness of either seeing Him or being seen by Him, leading to the stations of mushahada and muraqaba.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you stand in prayer, do you ever feel as if you are seeing Allah with your heart? If not, what is the cause? Will you today sincerely ask Allah to grant you a glimpse of His majesty in your worship?
?
You know that Allah sees you at every moment. Yet, when you sin alone, what makes you forget? Will you, from this lesson forward, pause before each action and remind yourself: 'He sees me'?
?
The hadith gives you two stations: one of seeing, one of being seen. Which one do you truly live by? If you are satisfied with mere vigilance while witnessing is possible, what does that say about your longing for Allah? Will you seek to elevate your soul?

Fana' and the Blameworthy Attributes
Al-Sawi defines fana' and lists blameworthy attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that fana' is the complete removal of blameworthy attributes from the soul, and you will recognize the specific traits that must be eliminated.

Core Idea
Fana' is not death but the soul's purification from ugly traits.

Al-Sawi begins by describing a high spiritual station that can only be reached through fana'. He defines fana' as the total removal of blameworthy attributes and then lists those traits. This lesson focuses on understanding fana' and identifying the qualities that hinder spiritual progress.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the station
Read the first part of the passage where Al-Sawi describes the station with successive divine openings and manifestations. Notice that this station requires perfection and purity of the soul.
2
Understand the definition of fana'
Find the definition: 'which is the complete removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul.' Note that it is not physical annihilation but moral purification.
The soul abstains from these traits as it would from eating carrion.
3
Review the list of blameworthy attributes
Go through each blameworthy attribute listed: envy, malice, love of status, reputation, praise, leadership, desires, pride, ostentation, self-admiration, hypocrisy, conceit, and hatred without religious cause. Reflect on how each one hinders spiritual growth.
This list is comprehensive and covers both internal vices and social faults.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا المقام تترادف فيه الفتوحات، وتعظم التَّجلّيات، وتتم المشاهدات والكشوفات ؛ لكمال النَّفْس وحُسن صفائها، ولا يمكن الوصول إليه إلا بعد الفناء، وهو زوالُ صفات النَّفس المذمومة بالكلية، حتّى لا تصير ملتفتة إلى شيء منها بل تزهدها كما تزهد أكل الجيفة مثلاً . وصفاتها المذمومة : الحسد والحقد، وحبُّ الجاهِ والصِّيتِ والمَحمدةِ والرِّياسةِ والشَّهواتِ والكِبرُ ، والرِّياءُ، والعُجب، والنّفاقُ، والغرور، وبغضُ أحدٍ من الخلق لغير غَرَض شرعيّ ونحو ذلك . فإذا زالت عنه هذه الأوصاف القبيحة اتّصف بأضدادها من الصِّفات الحميدة كالشَّفَقةِ والرَّأفة على الخَلْق، حتّى يحبّ لغيره ما يحب لنفسه، والإخلاص وحُسنِ الخُلُق والسَّخاء والمسكنة التي طلبها النَّبيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله : «اللهم أحيني مسكيناً، وأمتني مسكيناً، واحشرني في زمرة المساكين» (١) ، وهذه المسكنة هي : خضوع النَّفْس لمقام الألوهيَّة وخَفْضُ الجناح للبريَّة حتّى لا يشم صاحبها للرِّياسة رائحةً، وصاحبُها هو العبد الحقيقي الصِّدِّيق، فمن لم يتّصف بها لم تَخْلُ نفسه من منازعة الحقِّ تعالى. قوله : (لكمال النَّفس ) : علَّة لقوله : (وهذا المقام تترادف . . . إلخ . قوله : (والصيت) : أي : الشُّهرة بين النَّاس. قوله : (هي: خضوع النَّفس لمقام الألوهية ... إلخ) : أي : لأنَّ قصارى أمر العبد عدم وآيل إليه .
And this station is where divine openings (futuhat) are successive, and the manifestations (tajalliyat) are great, and the visions and unveilings are completed; due to the perfection of the soul and the goodness of its purity. And it cannot be reached except after fana' (annihilation), which is the complete removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul, so that it does not turn to any of them but rather abstains from them as it would abstain from eating carrion, for example. And its blameworthy attributes are: envy, malice, love of status, reputation, praise, leadership, desires, pride, ostentation, self-admiration, hypocrisy, conceit, and hatred of any of creation for no religious reason, and so on. So when these ugly attributes are removed from him, he becomes characterized by their opposites from the praiseworthy attributes: compassion, kindness to creation, so that he loves for others what he loves for himself, sincerity, good character, generosity, and maskanah (humility) which the Prophet asked for by his saying: 'O Allah, make me live as a poor person, die as a poor person, and resurrect me among the poor.' And this maskanah is: the soul's submission to the station of divinity and lowering the wing to creation so that its owner does not even smell the scent of leadership. And its owner is the true slave, the siddiq. So whoever is not characterized by it, his soul is not free from contending with the Truth, exalted. He said: (Due to the perfection of the soul): It is a cause for his saying: (And this station is successive... etc.). He said: (And reputation): meaning fame among people. He said: (It is: the soul's submission to the station of divinity... etc.): meaning that the ultimate end of the slave is non-existence and return to Him.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanation of the station of siddiqiyya and its prerequisites. It begins by describing the station itself: it is marked by successive divine openings, great manifestations, and complete visions and unveilings. This is achieved through perfection and purity of the soul. The key to this station is fana' (annihilation), defined as the complete removal of blameworthy attributes—such that the soul no longer inclines toward them but abhors them. A detailed list of blameworthy attributes is given: envy, malice, love of status, reputation, praise, leadership, desires, pride, ostentation, self-admiration, hypocrisy, conceit, and hatred without religious cause. When these are removed, the soul becomes adorned with their opposites: compassion, kindness to creation (including loving for others what one loves for oneself), sincerity, good character, generosity, and maskanah (humility). The Prophet's prayer for maskanah is cited, and maskanah is defined as the soul's submission to divinity and lowering one's wing to people, to the point of having no trace of desire for leadership. The one who embodies this is the true slave, the siddiq. The remainder of the passage is the commentator's explanatory remarks: 'due to the perfection of the soul' is a cause for the preceding description; 'reputation' means fame; and 'it is the soul's submission...' means the servant's ultimate end is non-existence and return to Allah.

Key Terms
فناء
صفات مذمومة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fana' means physical death or loss of consciousness.
Correction: Al-Sawi explicitly defines fana' as 'the complete removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul,' not physical annihilation.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Sawi, what is fana'?
A) Physical death
B) Complete removal of blameworthy attributes
C) Annihilation of the soul's existence
D) A state of trance

Key Takeaway
Fana' is the complete removal of blameworthy attributes from the soul, a prerequisite for reaching the highest spiritual station.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which blameworthy attribute from the list do you find yourself most attached to, and why is it difficult for you to detest it like carrion? What step will you take this week to uproot it?
?
You may claim to desire spiritual elevation, but are you willing to give up love of praise and leadership entirely? What would that cost you, and are you ready to pay that price?
?
The passage says the soul must not even be inclined towards these traits. Where in your daily life do you secretly enjoy a little status or admiration? How will you recognize and abandon that today?

Maskanah and the Praiseworthy Attributes
Al-Sawi lists praiseworthy attributes and defines maskanah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the praiseworthy attributes that replace blameworthy ones after fana', with special focus on maskanah and its definition as the soul's humility before Allah and creation.

Core Idea
Maskanah is the soul's humility before Allah and towards creation.

After fana', the soul acquires praiseworthy opposites. Al-Sawi highlights several, but emphasizes maskanah, which the Prophet himself sought. This lesson explores the nature of maskanah and why it is essential for the true servant of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the praiseworthy attributes listed
Read from 'فإذا زالت' to the end. Note the attributes: compassion, kindness, loving for others what one loves for oneself, sincerity, good character, generosity, and maskanah.
2
Understand the definition of maskanah
Find Al-Sawi's definition: 'the soul's submission to the station of divinity and lowering the wing to creation.' Reflect on how this involves humility towards Allah and people.
The Prophet's prayer shows its importance.
3
Reflect on the consequence of lacking maskanah
The text says that without it, one's soul is not free from contending with the Truth. Consider why maskanah is so crucial.

The State of Fana and Blameworthy Qualities
Description of fana state, blameworthy and commendable qualities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of fana as the complete removal of blameworthy qualities and the subsequent acquisition of commendable qualities, especially humility (maskanah).

Core Idea
True spiritual annihilation is the removal of blameworthy qualities, not the destruction of the self.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Sawi explains a key stage on the spiritual path: the state of fana. It clarifies that this annihilation means the complete stripping away of blameworthy traits like envy and arrogance. Once these are gone, the soul naturally acquires their opposites, culminating in the profound humility known as maskanah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic original and then the English translation to get an overview of the content.
Pay attention to the flow from definition to enumeration to transformation.
2
Identify the definition of fana
Locate the explicit definition of fana and note the vivid comparison to abandoning a carcass.
This shows the total aversion to blameworthy qualities.
3
List the blameworthy qualities
Find the list of blameworthy qualities (e.g., envy, hatred, love of status) and understand each term.
This list is key to recognizing what must be removed.
4
Understand maskanah
Focus on the definition of humility (maskanah) and its connection to the Prophet's hadith.
Maskanah is presented as the pinnacle of commendable qualities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشاهدات والكشوفات ؛ لكمال النَّفْس وحُسن صفائها، ولا يمكن الوصول إليه إلا بعد الفناء، وهو زوالُ صفات النَّفس المذمومة بالكلية، حتّى لا تصير ملتفتة إلى شيء منها بل تزهدها كما تزهد أكل الجيفة مثلاً . هي. وصفاتها المذمومة : الحسد والحقد، وحبُّ الجاهِ والصِّيتِ والمَحمدةِ والرِّياسةِ والشَّهواتِ والكِبرُ ، والرِّياءُ، والعُجب، والنّفاقُ، والغرور، وبغضُ أحدٍ من الخلق لغير غَرَض شرعيّ ونحو ذلك . فإذا زالت عنه هذه الأوصاف القبيحة اتّصف بأضدادها من الصِّفات الحميدة كالشَّفَقةِ والرَّأفة على الخَلْق، حتّى يحبّ لغيره ما يحب لنفسه، والإخلاص وحُسنِ الخُلُق والسَّخاء والمسكنة التي طلبها النَّبيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله : «اللهم أحيني مسكيناً، وأمتني مسكيناً، واحشرني في زمرة المساكين» (١) ، وهذه المسكنة هي : خضوع النَّفْس لمقام الألوهيَّة وخَفْضُ الجناح للبريَّة حتّى لا يشم صاحبها للرِّياسة رائحةً، وصاحبُها هو العبد الحقيقي الصِّدِّيق، فمن لم يتّصف بها لم تَخْلُ نفسه من منازعة الحقِّ تعالى.
قوله : (لكمال النَّفس ) : علَّة لقوله : (وهذا المقام تترادف . . . إلخ .
قوله : (والصيت) : أي : الشُّهرة بين النَّاس.
قوله : (هي: خضوع النَّفس لمقام الألوهية ... إلخ) : أي : لأنَّ قصارى أمر العبد عدم وآيل إليه .
The observations and unveilings; for the perfection of the soul and the beauty of its purity, and it cannot be reached except after annihilation (al-fana'), which is the complete removal of the blameworthy qualities of the soul, so that it does not turn to anything of them but rather abandons them as one abandons eating a carcass, for example. It (i.e., the soul). And its blameworthy qualities are: envy, spite, love of status, fame, praise, leadership, desires, arrogance, hypocrisy, self-conceit, deceit, hatred of any of creation without a legitimate religious purpose, and the like. So when these ugly attributes leave him, he becomes characterized by their opposites of praiseworthy qualities such as compassion and mercy towards creation, so that he loves for others what he loves for himself, and sincerity, good character, generosity, and humility (al-maskanah) which the Prophet, God bless him and grant him peace, asked for by saying: 'O God, let me live humble, die humble, and gather me among the humble.' (1) And this humility (al-maskanah) is: the soul's submission to the station of divinity and lowering the wing to creation so that its owner does not smell any scent of leadership, and its owner is the true servant, the veracious (al-siddiq). Whoever is not characterized by it, his soul is not free from contending with God Most High. His saying: '(For the perfection of the soul)': a cause for his saying: 'And this station is synonymous... etc.' His saying: '(and fame)': i.e., renown among people. His saying: '(It is: the soul's submission to the station of divinity... etc.)': i.e., because the ultimate end of the servant is non-existence and it returns to Him.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage explains the state of fana (annihilation) and describes the blameworthy and commendable qualities of the soul. It begins by stating that the spiritual observations and unveilings are attained after achieving fana, which is the complete removal of blameworthy qualities. The author then lists these blameworthy qualities: envy, spite, love of status, fame, praise, leadership, desires, arrogance, hypocrisy, self-conceit, deceit, and unjustified hatred. Once these are removed, the soul acquires their opposites: compassion, mercy, sincerity, good character, generosity, and humility (maskanah). The passage highlights humility through the Prophet's hadith. The author defines maskanah as submission to God and lowering one's wing to people, so that no trace of desire for leadership remains. The one who possesses this is the true servant and veracious. The commentary that follows clarifies that 'perfection of the soul' is a reason for the preceding statement, 'fame' means renown, and the definition of maskanah implies the servant's ultimate end is non-existence before God.

الصفات المذمومة
الصفات الحميدة
المسكنة
التحقق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think fana means literal annihilation of the self or destruction of the soul's essence.
Correction: The passage clearly states that fana is the complete removal of blameworthy qualities, not the annihilation of the soul itself.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of fana (annihilation) according to this passage?
A) The complete removal of blameworthy qualities of the soul.
B) The death of the physical body.
C) The attainment of worldly leadership.
D) The acquisition of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Fana is the complete removal of blameworthy qualities, leading to humility (maskanah) which is the essence of true servanthood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the blameworthy qualities listed in this passage do you find most deeply rooted in your own heart? Reflect on why you cling to it and what step you will take today to begin removing it.
?
The passage says that when these qualities are removed, you love for others what you love for yourself. Is there a specific person for whom you do not wish the good you wish for yourself? What does that reveal about the state of your soul?
?
The Prophet asked to live and die humble. How would your daily habits change if you truly lived with the maskanah described here? What is one area where you are most defensive or proud, and how can you actively lower your wing to creation today?

The Path to Pure Servitude: Dhikr, Struggle, and the Five Pillars
Description of the path to pure servitude: dhikr, hunger, seclusion, silence, and five pillars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practical path to pure servitude (al-‘ubudiyya al-mahda) and the five pillars that support it.

Core Idea
Pure servitude requires struggling against the love of leadership and embracing a disciplined path.

This passage from the commentary on al-Kharida describes the struggle to attain pure servitude to Allah. It highlights the last impurity to leave the soul—love of leadership—and outlines a transformative journey of dhikr, hunger, seclusion, silence, and five essential pillars. Let's explore these teachings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first obstacle: love of leadership
Read the opening lines about leadership belonging only to God and how it is the last thing to leave the truthful. Understand why this is significant.
This shows that purification is a gradual process.
2
Learn the core practices of dhikr and mujahada
Focus on the description of constant dhikr, heart attachment, hunger, sleeplessness, seclusion, and silence. Notice the Quranic verse cited (29:69).
3
Understand the five remaining pillars
From the commentary, note the five pillars: renewal of repentance, gratitude, patience, reflection, and the spiritual guide.
4
Reflect on the role of the spiritual guide
Consider why the shaykh al-‘arif is included as a pillar. This emphasizes the need for a teacher.
This is a crucial aspect of the path.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الذاكر
[10]
أخص أوصافه ؛ لأنَّ الرِّياسة إنَّما تكون للفاعل المختار الغني على الإطلاق، وهي لا تفارق الإنسان إلا بعد المجاهدة الكبرى، فَعِرْقُها لا ينقطع عن أحد إلا من خصَّه الله بالعبودية المحضة، ولذا قالوا : آخر ما يخرج من قلب الصِّدِّقين حبُّ الرِّياسة .
الطريق الموصلة إلى مقام العبودية المحضة
ولا يسهل الوصول إليها عادة إلا بمداومة ذكر (لا إله إلّا الله ليلاً ونهاراً، مع تعلق القلب بالله وحده، والجوع والشهر، والاعتزال عن النَّاس ، والصَّمت إلا عن ذكر الله تعالى وملاحظة بقيَّة أركان الطريق التي سيأتي بيانها إن شاء الله تعالى وهو المسمى بالمجاهدة، قال تعالى: وَالَّذِينَ جَهَدُوا فِينَا لَنَهْدِيَنَّهُمْ سُبُلَنَا (١)، وهذا الترقي هو المسمَّى ( بالسُّلوك إلى ملك الملوك عند الطائفة )
قوله : (في أخصّ أوصافه) : أي : وهي العظمة والكبرياء؛ لما الحديث : «العظمةُ ،إزاري، والكبرياء ردائي، فمن نازعني في شيء منهما قصمته (۲)
قوله : (إِنَّما تكون للفاعل المختار) : أي : وهو الله تعالى.
قوله : ( وملاحظة بقيَّة أركان الطَّريق ... إلخ) : أي : وهي خمسة تجديد التّوبة، والشكر والصبر، والفكر، والشيخ العارف.
The etiquette of the one who remembers God.
[10]
His most specific attributes; because leadership belongs only to the free-acting agent, the absolutely self-sufficient, and it does not leave a person except after the great struggle; its vein does not cease from anyone except the one whom God has specially favored with pure servitude. Therefore they said: The last thing to leave the hearts of the truthful is love of leadership.
The paths leading to the station of pure servitude.
And it is not usually easy to reach it except by continuous remembrance of 'There is no god but God' night and day, with the heart's attachment to God alone, hunger, sleeplessness, withdrawal from people, silence except for the remembrance of God, and observing the remaining pillars of the path which will be explained, God willing, and this is called the struggle (mujahada). God said: 'And those who strive in Us, We will surely guide them to Our paths' (1). And this ascension is called the journey to the King of Kings among the folk (al-ta'ifa).
His saying: '(His most specific attributes)': i.e., magnificence and grandeur; because of the hadith: 'Magnificence is My lower garment, and Grandeur is My cloak; whoever contends with Me in either of them, I will break him.' (2)
His saying: '(It belongs only to the free-acting agent)': i.e., He is God Most High.
His saying: '(and observing the remaining pillars of the path... etc.)': i.e., they are five: renewal of repentance, gratitude, patience, reflection, and the spiritual guide (al-shaykh al-‘arif).
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage describes the path to pure servitude (al-‘ubudiyya al-mahda). It begins by stating that leadership (al-riyasa) belongs only to God, the free-acting and self-sufficient, and it leaves a person only after great struggle. The last thing to leave the hearts of the truthful is the love of leadership. Then it outlines the path: constant dhikr of 'La ilaha illa Allah' with heart attachment, hunger, sleeplessness, seclusion, silence except for dhikr, and observing the remaining pillars. This path is called mujahada (struggle), citing Quran 29:69. This ascension is called the journey to the King of Kings among the spiritual folk. The commentary explains that 'most specific attributes' refer to God's magnificence and grandeur, citing a hadith. The phrase 'belongs only to the free-acting agent' refers to God. The 'remaining pillars' are five: renewal of repentance, gratitude, patience, reflection, and the spiritual guide (the knower of God).

Key Terms
العبودية المحضة
المجاهدة
الذكر
الخمسة أركان
الشيخ العارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think love of leadership is always evil; but here it is attributed exclusively to God, and its love is the last impurity to leave the soul.
Correction: Leadership itself is a divine attribute; humans should not seek it but purify their hearts from attachment to it.

Checkpoint

A) Remembrance, hunger, seclusion, silence, and struggle.
B) Renewal of repentance, gratitude, patience, reflection, and the spiritual guide.
C) Love, fear, hope, trust, and sincerity.

Key Takeaway
Pure servitude is attained through a disciplined struggle that combines external practices with inner pillars, guided by a spiritual teacher.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The path demands silence except for dhikr. When was the last time you spent an hour in complete silence, with your heart clinging to God alone? What prevents you from starting tonight?
?
Of the five inner pillars—repentance, gratitude, patience, reflection, and a spiritual guide—which one are you actively ignoring, and what is the first concrete step you will take this week to revive it?

The Most Special Attribute and the Root of Love of Leadership
Explains the divine attribute of grandeur and the root of love of leadership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the most special divine attributes are majesty and grandeur, and that love of leadership is a deep-rooted trait that can only be purified through spiritual struggle and divine grace.

Core Idea
Love of leadership is the last vice to leave the sincere heart.

This lesson explores a profound spiritual insight: the love of leadership is the most stubborn attachment of the human soul, and it is rooted in the fact that true leadership belongs only to God. The passage explains that this attribute of grandeur (al-ʿaẓama) and majesty (al-kibriyāʾ) is unique to Allah, and that sincere seekers must struggle to uproot any claim to it. The hadith of the divine garments powerfully illustrates this exclusive possession.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then read the literal English translation. Notice the concise style and the key terms.
2
Understand the nature of leadership as divine
The passage states that leadership (al-riyāsa) belongs only to the 'freely acting agent, the absolutely self-sufficient' – that is, Allah. This sets the stage for why humans struggle with the desire for it.
Consider why leadership is considered an attribute of God before a human ambition.
3
Reflect on the hadith about majesty and grandeur
The hadith 'Majesty is My lower garment, and grandeur is My cloak…' powerfully illustrates that these traits belong exclusively to God. Whoever claims them is in opposition to Him.
This hadith is often cited in Sufi literature to emphasize tawḥīd in attributes.

Source Text

آداب الذاكر

أخص أوصافه ؛ لأنَّ الرِّياسة إنَّما تكون للفاعل المختار الغني على الإطلاق، وهي لا تفارق الإنسان إلا بعد المجاهدة الكبرى، فَعِرْقُها لا ينقطع عن أحد إلا من خصَّه الله بالعبودية المحضة، ولذا قالوا : آخر ما يخرج من قلب الصِّدِّقين حبُّ الرِّياسة .

The etiquette of the rememberer [10] Most special of His attributes: because leadership is only for the freely acting agent, the absolutely self-sufficient, and it does not leave a person except after the great struggle; its root does not cease from anyone except whom God has singled out for pure servitude. Hence they said: The last thing to exit from the hearts of the truthful is love of leadership. Commentary
This passage defines the most special divine attribute as majesty and grandeur and explains why love of leadership clings to humans. It first states that leadership belongs exclusively to the freely acting agent who is absolutely self-sufficient — i.e., God. Then it notes that this attribute does not leave a person except after great spiritual struggle (mujahada). The root of this love is only cut off from one whom God has singled out for pure servitude. The author quotes a saying: 'The last thing to exit the hearts of the truthful is love of leadership.' Then the commentary clarifies that by 'most special of His attributes' the text means majesty and grandeur, citing the prophetic hadith that these are God's exclusive garments. Finally, it affirms that 'the freely acting agent' referred to is God Almighty.

The Prophetic and Non-Prophetic Spiritual Paths
Describes the different starting points and ends of prophetic and non-prophetic spiritual paths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the starting points and ends of prophetic and non-prophetic spiritual paths, and why the Prophet Muhammad's path is unique.

Core Idea
Prophets start from perfection; others start from darkness.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary contrasts the spiritual journeys of prophets and ordinary believers. It reveals that prophets begin their ascent from already purified souls, while others start from lower soul states. The key insight is that the end result depends on the starting point, and the Prophet Muhammad's beginning is the end of others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to get the overall contrast between prophetic and non-prophetic paths.
The passage includes commentary glosses; focus on the main text first.
2
Identify the two starting points
Notice that prophets begin from 'purified perfect souls' while others begin from 'dark commanding or blaming souls'. This is the fundamental difference.
3
Understand the graded nature of the prophetic path
The prophets' path itself is differentiated: the higher prophets (ulu al-azm) have a higher path, and the Prophet Muhammad is the highest since his start is the end of others.
This shows the superiority of the Prophet Muhammad.
4
Apply the principle: beginnings determine ends
Note the principle that the illumination of the end depends on the beginning. 'Burning the beginning' through struggle leads to knowledge and secrets.
Reflect on how this applies to spiritual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فسلوك الأنبياء عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام مبدؤه التَّرقي من نفوس مطهَّرة كمالية إلى ما لا نهاية له من المقامات الإحسانية، وهو في نفسه متفاوت، فسلوكُ أُولي العزم منهم أعلى وأجلُّ من سلوك غيرهم، وسلوك سيّد أُولي العزم عليه وعليهم أفضل الصَّلاة والسَّلام أعلى من غيره، إذ مبدؤه نهاية غيره .
- وأما سلوك غيرهم : فمن نفوس أمارة أو لوّامة ظلمانيَّة، إلى نفس كاملة صدّيقيَّة .
والنّهايات تختلف في الإشراق بحسب اختلاف البدايات، فبإحراق البداية يكون إشراق النهاية .
قوله : (وهو في نفسه متفاوت) : أي : فالسلوك مقول بالتشكيك .
قوله : (نهاية غيره أي من أولي العزم.
قوله: (والنهايات تختلف . . . إلخ) أي نهايات غير الأنبياء عليهم السلام.
قوله : ( فبإحراق البداية أي بالمجاهدة بالذّكر والفكر .
وقوله : (يكون إشراق النّهاية أي بالعلوم والمعارف، والأسرار.
The path of the prophets, peace be upon them, has its beginning in ascent from purified perfect souls to endless stations of excellence, and it is in itself differentiated; thus the path of the possessors of resolve among them is higher and greater than the path of others, and the path of the master of the possessors of resolve, peace be upon him and them, is higher than others, since its beginning is the end of others. As for the path of others: it is from dark commanding or blaming souls to a complete truthful soul. The ends differ in illumination according to the difference of beginnings; by burning the beginning, the illumination of the end occurs. He said (and it is in itself differentiated): meaning the path is said by analogy (bi-al-tashkik). He said (the end of others): meaning from the possessors of resolve. He said (and the ends differ... etc.): meaning the ends of other than the prophets, peace be upon them. He said (by burning the beginning): meaning by struggle through remembrance and reflection. And he said (the illumination of the end occurs): meaning by sciences, knowledges, and secrets.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage contrasts the spiritual paths of prophets and others. It explains that prophets begin their spiritual journey from already purified perfect souls, ascending to infinite ranks. Their path itself is graded, with the 'possessors of resolve' (ulu al-azm, the major prophets) having a higher path, and the Prophet Muhammad being the highest of all, as his starting point is the end of others. Non-prophets, in contrast, begin from lower soul states—either the commanding soul (al-ammara) or the blaming soul (al-lawwama)—which are dark, and they aim to reach a perfect truthful soul (nafs kāmila siddīqiyya). The key principle is that the end result (illumination) differs based on the starting point. The commentary gloss clarifies that 'burning the beginning' refers to spiritual struggle (mujāhada) through dhikr and reflection, and the 'illumination of the end' refers to knowledge, gnosis, and secrets.

Key Terms
النفس الأمارة
النفس اللوامة
أولو العزم
التشكيك
المجاهدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all spiritual paths begin from the same starting point.
Correction: This passage clarifies that prophets start from purified souls, while others start from lower souls. The ends differ accordingly.

Checkpoint

A) From dark commanding souls.
B) From purified perfect souls.
C) From the blaming soul.
D) From the complete truthful soul.

Key Takeaway
The spiritual path of prophets begins from perfection, while others begin from imperfection, and the end result is determined by the starting point and the effort of spiritual struggle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul today—is it commanding you towards sin (ammara), blaming you after sin (lawwama), or at peace? Which description fits you right now, and what does that reveal about your starting point? Are you willing to face this truth and begin the struggle (mujahada) to transform it?
?
The prophets began from purity; you began from darkness. Does that reality humble you or discourage you? How does the promise of reaching a 'complete truthful soul (nafs kamila siddiqiyya)' change the way you approach your own spiritual struggle today? Will you commit to ‘burning your beginning’ through consistent dhikr and reflection, even when it feels hopeless?
?
The Prophet Muhammad's beginning was the end of others. If you truly believed that his path is incomparably higher, would you still follow it with the same eagerness? What keeps you from longing for his way more than your own way? Are you willing to abandon your own lower starting point and cling completely to his example?

The Seven Souls and Threefold Classification
Reconciles seven souls (Khalwati) with three souls (Shadhili).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the threefold Shadhili classification of the soul and how it incorporates the sevenfold Khalwati schema without contradiction.

Core Idea
Different Sufi orders classify souls differently, but their stages are compatible.

This passage addresses a seeming discrepancy between two Sufi orders regarding the number of soul stages. The Khalwatiyya list seven souls, while the Shadhiliyya list only three. The author shows that the differences are merely in naming and subdivision, not in essence. Let us explore how.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by stating the two classifications and then explains the reconciliation.
2
Identify the two classifications
Find the seven souls in the Khalwatiyya schema and the three souls in the Shadhiliyya schema. Note which souls are subsumed.
The key terms list the seven names; the Shadhili three are the commanding, blaming, and tranquil.
3
Understand the reconciliation argument
The passage explains that the inspired soul is included in the blaming soul when blame intensifies. Then the well-pleasing, pleased, and complete souls are included in the tranquil soul as it ascends. This shows the compatibility.
Focus on the reasoning: 'when blame increases...' and 'when it ascends in perfections...'
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider why different orders might enumerate differently. The author's conclusion 'so there is no disagreement between them' teaches us to look for underlying unity in apparent diversity.
This principle applies beyond this specific case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والنُّفوس سبعة ) : أي : عند السادة الخلوتية، وأما عند السادة الشاذلية فثلاثة ،أمارة ولوامة، ومطمئنة فأدخلوا الملهمة في اللَّوَّامة، وأدخلوا المرضية والراضية والكاملة في المطمئنة
ووجه ذلك : أنَّ النَّفس النَّوَّامة إذا كثر منها اللوم؛ صارت عيوبها بين عينيها، فاشتغلت بها عن غيرها وهي الملهمة، وأنَّ المطمئنة إذا ترفَّت الكمالات؛ رضيت بما قضاه الله وقدره، فجوزيت بالرضا من خالقها، فإذا زاد ترقّيها كملت فهذه مطمئنة وزيادة، فلا خلاف بينهم.
He said (and the souls are seven): meaning according to the masters of the Khalwatiyya. As for according to the masters of the Shadhiliyya, they are three: the commanding, the blaming, and the tranquil. So they included the inspired in the blaming, and they included the well-pleasing, the pleased, and the complete in the tranquil. And the explanation for that is that the blaming soul (al-nawwāma) when blame increases in it, its faults become before its eyes, so it becomes occupied with them to the exclusion of others, and it is the inspired. And that the tranquil soul when it ascends in perfections, it is pleased with what God has decreed and determined, so it is recompensed with pleasure from its Creator. Then when its ascent increases, it becomes complete; so this is tranquil and more. So there is no disagreement between them.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential contradiction between two Sufi orders in enumerating the soul stages. The Khalwatiyya hold that there are seven souls (as per their schema), while the Shadhiliyya hold there are three: the commanding (ammara), the blaming (lawwama), and the tranquil (mutma'innah). The author reconciles this by showing that the Shadhiliyya subsume the intermediate 'inspired' soul (mulhama) within the blaming soul, and the higher 'well-pleasing' (mardiyya), 'pleased' (radiyya), and 'complete' (kāmila) within the tranquil soul. The explanation is that when the blaming soul's self-reproach intensifies, it becomes acutely aware of its faults and is thus inspired, so it is included in the blaming stage. The tranquil soul, when it perfects itself, is pleased with divine decree and is recompensed with divine pleasure; further ascent makes it complete. Thus, the difference is only in naming and subdivision, not in reality, so there is no conflict.

Key Terms
النفس الأمارة
النفس اللوامة
النفس المطمئنة
النفس الملهمة
النفس المرضية
النفس الراضية
النفس الكاملة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khalwatiyya and Shadhiliyya enumerations of soul stages are contradictory.
Correction: The Shadhiliyya classification of three souls is compatible with the Khalwatiyya's seven because the inspired and the higher three are subsumed under the blaming and tranquil souls respectively.

Checkpoint
How do the Shadhiliyya treat the 'inspired soul' (mulhama) in their threefold classification?
A) They include it in the commanding soul.
B) They include it in the tranquil soul.
C) They include it in the blaming soul.
D) They consider it a separate fourth soul.

Key Takeaway
The different enumerations of soul stages in Sufi orders are not contradictory but represent different levels of detail.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The blaming soul, when it intensifies self-reproach, sees its faults clearly. When was the last moment you honestly confronted a fault of yours without making excuses? Did that confrontation lead you to change, or did you quickly move on?
?
The tranquil soul is pleased with Allah's decree. Is there a situation in your life right now where you are struggling to accept what Allah has willed? What would it take for you to genuinely say 'I am pleased'?
?
This lesson shows that different spiritual classifications can be reconciled. In your own spiritual journey, do you hold onto differences in terminology or method at the expense of the essence? What would it mean for you to seek the underlying truth rather than getting caught in surface-level disagreements?

The Commanding and Blaming Souls
Defines two types of soul with description and Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics of the commanding soul and how it transforms into the blaming soul through struggle and self-reproach.

Core Idea
The soul progresses from pure evil to self-awareness through struggle.

Sanusi begins describing the sevenfold classification of the soul with the first two: the commanding soul and the blaming soul. This passage explains their nature, how they relate to Quranic verses, and the subtle reality that even a seemingly good act like jihad can stem from a selfish soul. Understanding these states is crucial for recognizing the inner struggle (jihad al-nafs).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to get a sense of the content. Note the Quranic references.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify the two souls and their definitions
The passage defines the commanding soul first, then explains how it becomes the blaming soul. Notice the condition for transformation: struggle and submission, but still dominating, then returning with blame.
3
Analyze the story of the man and jihad
The commentary includes a story about a man whose soul commanded him to jihad to seek death and rest. Reflect on how this shows that even religious acts can have hidden selfish motives.
The story is in the commentary, not the source text, but it is part of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the key terms
Note the Arabic terms: النفس الأمارة and النفس اللوامة. Understand their Quranic origins and implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأولى : النَّفس الأمارة بالسُّوء، وهي التي لا تأمر صاحبها بخير. فإذا جاهدها صاحبها وخالفها في شهواتها حتى أذعنت لاتِّباع الحقِّ، وسكنت تحت الأمر التكليفي، ولكنها تغلب صاحبها في أكثر أحوالها، ثم ترجع إليه باللوم على ما وقع سُمِّيت لوّامة، وهي الثانية .
قوله : (الأولى : النفس الأمارة وهي مأخوذة من قوله تعالى : إِنَّ النَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ ) (١) .
قوله : (لا) تأمر صاحبها بخير) أي خالص من العلل، فلا ينافي قد تأمر بخير معلول كما اتفق لرجل أمرته نفسه بالجهاد يوماً، فطلب الله أن يطلعه على دسائسها ، فأطلعه الله على أنّها تريد أن تجاهد وتقتل مرَّة واحدة؛ لتستريح من قتلك لها كذا كذا مرَّة.
قوله: (سمِّيت لوّامة، وهي الثَّانية) : أي : وهي مأخوذة من قوله تعالى: وَلَا أُقْسِمُ بِالنَّفْسِ اللَّوَّامَةِ ) (۲)
The first: the soul that commands evil, which does not command its possessor to do good. When its possessor struggles against it and opposes it in its desires until it submits to following the truth and settles under the command of obligation, but it overcomes its possessor in most of its states, then it returns to him with blame for what happened—it is called the blaming soul, and it is the second. He said (the first: the commanding soul, and it is taken from His statement, Exalted: 'Indeed the soul is a persistent commander of evil' (1). He said ('does not command its possessor to do good') meaning pure good, free from defects, so it does not contradict that it may command a defective good, as happened with a man whose soul commanded him to do jihad one day, so he asked God to show him its hidden plots, so God showed him that it wanted to wage jihad and be killed once, to be relieved from your killing it so many times. He said ('it is called the blaming soul, and it is the second') meaning it is taken from His statement, Exalted: 'And I swear by the blaming soul' (2).
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed definition of the first two souls in the sevenfold classification. The first is the commanding soul (al-nafs al-ammāra bi al-sū'), which by nature commands only evil and never commands pure good. The commentary clarifies that 'does not command good' means good that is free from hidden defects—it may appear to command a good deed like jihad, but the underlying motive is selfish. A story illustrates this: a man was commanded by his soul to fight so it could die once and be free from repeated struggle. When a person struggles against this soul and opposes its desires, it eventually submits outwardly and obeys religious obligations, but still dominates in most of his states. Once it begins to blame him for its own failures, it transforms into the second soul, the blaming soul (al-lawwāma). This state is named after the Quranic verse 'I swear by the blaming soul.' The passage thus shows the progressive refinement of the soul from pure evil to self-awareness and reproach.

Key Terms
النفس الأمارة
النفس اللوامة
الجهاد
الشهوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the commanding soul never commands any good at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies it can command a defective good with hidden selfish motives, as shown in the jihad story.

Checkpoint
What triggers the transformation of the commanding soul into the blaming soul?
A) When it completely stops desiring evil.
B) When it struggles against desires and submits, but then returns to blame itself.
C) When it receives divine inspiration.
D) When it attains tranquility.

Key Takeaway
The commanding soul can only be transformed into the blaming soul through continual struggle and self-reproach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you did something that looked good outwardly, like helping someone or performing an act of worship, but deep down you knew your intention was not purely for Allah. How did your 'commanding soul' deceive you, and what will you do next time to expose its hidden plot before acting?
?
The blaming soul reproaches itself after failing. When you fall into sin despite your efforts, does your self-blame push you towards genuine change, or does it become a cycle of guilt without transformation? What one concrete step can you take today to break that cycle?
?
In the story, the man asked Allah to reveal the hidden motives of his soul. When was the last time you sincerely asked Allah to show you the true state of your heart before you acted? If you haven't, what is stopping you from making that supplication right now?

The Four Stages of the Soul: From Commanding Evil to Tranquility
Al-Sawi enumerates four stages of the soul with Quranic proofs and signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four stages of the soul (nafs) as described in Islamic spirituality, their Quranic foundations, and the signs of each stage.

Core Idea
The soul's journey through four stages mirrors the path to spiritual purification.

In this passage, Al-Sawi presents a detailed classification of the soul's states based on Quranic verses and Sufi tradition. He describes how the soul progresses from commanding evil, through blame and inspiration, to ultimate tranquility. This lesson will walk you through each stage, the Quranic proofs, and key signs that distinguish them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Get a sense of the flow from one soul type to the next.
Notice that the passage includes embedded commentary (قوله) which explains each type.
2
Identify each soul type and its Quranic proof
For each of the four souls, find the Quranic verse Al-Sawi cites. This grounds the classification in revelation.
The verses are from Surah Yusuf (12:53), Surah Al-Qiyamah (75:2), Surah Ash-Shams (91:8), and Surah Al-Fajr (89:27-30).
3
Examine the Shadhili classification and the inspired soul's danger
Al-Sawi explains how the Shadhili school reduces the four to three distinct types, and warns of the danger of the inspired stage requiring reliance on a shaykh.
This shows the nuanced differences between spiritual schools.

لوّامة، وهي الثَّانية) : أي : وهي مأخوذة من قوله تعالى: وَلَا أُقْسِمُ بِالنَّفْسِ اللَّوَّامَةِ ) (۲) فإذا أخذ في المجاهدة والكَدِّ، حتّى مالت إلى عالم القُدس واستنارت بحيث ألهمت فجورها وتقواها، سُمِّيت ملهمة، وهي الثالثة، وعلامتها أن يعرف صاحبها دسائسها الخفيَّة الدَّقيقة؛ من الرّياء والعجب وغير ذلك. فإذا لزم المجاهدة حتّى زالت عنها الشَّهوات، وتبدلت الصفات المذمومة بالمحمودة، وتخلّقت بأخلاق الله تعالى الجمالية؛ من الرّأفة والرَّحمة واللطف والكرم والوُدِّ سُمِّيت مطمئنة، وهي الرابعة، وهذا المقام هو مبدأ الوصول إلى الله تعالى ولكنَّها لا تخلو من دسائس وقوله : (سمِّيت ملهمة، وهي الثَّالثة) : أي : وهي مأخوذة من قوله تعالى: (فَأَهْمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَنَهَا (١) . قوله : ( وعلامتها أن يعرف صاحبها دسائسها الخفيَّة) ومن جملة علامتها : الشَّوق، والهيمان، والسكر، إذ هو في هذا المقام فان عمَّا سوى الله تعالى، ولكنَّ هذا المقام كثير العطب لا ينجو منه عادة إلا باستناده لشيخه بالكلية قوله : ( سميت مطمئنة، وهي الرَّابعة : هذه وما بعدها إلى السَّابعة مأخوذة من قوله تعالى : يَأَيّها النَّفْسُ الْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ارْجِعِي إِلَى رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةً فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَدِي وَادْخُلِي جَنَّنِي (٢) . قوله : ( هو مبدأ الوصول) : أي : ولذا يقولون: هو أول قدم يضعه
The first: the soul commanding evil, and it does not command its owner to good. Then if its owner struggles against it and opposes it in its desires until it yields to following the truth, and settles under the prescriptive command, but it overcomes its owner in most of its states, then it returns to him with blame for what occurred, it is called the blaming soul, and it is the second. The Shadhiliyya say three: commanding, blaming, and tranquil. So they included the inspired in the blaming, and they included the pleasing, the pleased, and the complete in the tranquil. And the explanation of that: that the blaming soul, when blame increases from it, its faults become between its eyes, so it occupies itself with them instead of other things, and that is the inspired. And that the tranquil soul, when it attains perfections, is pleased with what God has decreed and predestined, so it is recompensed with pleasure from its Creator. Then if its ascent increases, it becomes complete, so this is tranquil and more, so there is no disagreement between them. His saying: (The first: the commanding soul, and it is taken from His saying: 'Indeed the soul is constantly commanding evil') (1). His saying: ('does not') command its owner to good) meaning pure from defects, so it does not contradict that it may command a defective good, as happened to a man whose soul commanded him to jihad one day, so he asked God to show him its hidden schemes, so God showed him that it wanted to fight and be killed once, to rest from your killing it so many times. His saying: ('called blaming, and it is the second'): meaning it is taken from His saying: 'And I swear by the blaming soul') (2). Then if he takes up struggling and exertion until it inclines to the world of holiness and becomes illuminated such that it is inspired with its wickedness and piety, it is called the inspired soul, and it is the third. Its sign is that its owner knows its subtle hidden schemes, from showing off and vanity and other than that. Then if he persists in struggling until desires leave it, and blameworthy attributes are exchanged for praiseworthy ones, and it is adorned with the beautiful attributes of God Almighty, from compassion, mercy, kindness, generosity, and love, it is called the tranquil soul, and it is the fourth. This station is the beginning of arrival to God Almighty, but it is not free from hidden schemes. And His saying: ('called inspired, and it is the third'): meaning it is taken from His saying: 'Then He inspired it with its wickedness and piety') (1). His saying: ('and its sign is that its owner knows its subtle hidden schemes') and among its signs are: longing, bewilderment, and intoxication, for he is in this station annihilated from other than God, but this station is very dangerous, usually one is not saved from it except by total reliance on his shaykh. His saying: ('called tranquil, and it is the fourth): this and what follows up to the seventh are taken from His saying: 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, pleased and pleasing, and enter among My servants, and enter My Garden') (2). His saying: ('it is the beginning of arrival'): meaning, so they say: it is the first step he places
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the stages of the soul (nafs) as discussed in Sufi spiritual psychology, drawn from Quranic verses. The author enumerates four primary types, addresses the Shadhili school's alternative classification, and provides signs for each type. The passage follows a logical order: first the commanding soul (ammara), then the blaming soul (lawwama), then the inspired soul (mulhama), and finally the tranquil soul (mutma'innah). The author begins by defining the first type: the soul that commands evil, taken from the Quranic verse 'Indeed the soul is constantly commanding evil' (Q12:53). He clarifies that 'does not command its owner to good' means it commands no pure good, but it may command a defective good with hidden motives, illustrated by a story of a man whose soul incited him to jihad to be killed and thus escape further struggle. The second type, the blaming soul, is from the verse 'I swear by the blaming soul' (Q75:2). It arises when the owner struggles against the commanding soul until it submits but still often overcomes, leading to remorse. The author then notes that the Shadhili school recognizes only three types: commanding, blaming, and tranquil, subsuming the inspired soul under the blaming soul and the additional pleasing, pleased, and complete souls under the tranquil soul. He explains that the blaming soul, when blame increases, becomes aware of its faults and occupies itself with them—this is the inspired soul. Similarly, the tranquil soul, when perfected, is pleased with divine decree and receives divine pleasure; further ascent makes it complete—still tranquil but with increase. Thus there is no real disagreement. The third type, the inspired soul (mulhama), is from the verse 'Then He inspired it with its wickedness and piety' (Q91:8). It is reached through continued struggle until the soul inclines to the holy realm and is enlightened; its sign is that the person recognizes its subtle hidden schemes like showing off and vanity. The fourth type, the tranquil soul (mutma'innah), is from the verse 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord...' (Q89:27-30). It is attained when desires vanish and attributes become praiseworthy, reflecting God's beautiful attributes like mercy and kindness. This station is the beginning of arrival to God but still has hidden schemes. The author adds that in the inspired stage, signs include longing, bewilderment, and intoxication, and it is a dangerous station requiring total reliance on one's shaykh. The passage concludes that the tranquil soul and those up to the seventh are all taken from that same Quranic verse.

Key Terms
النفس الأمارة
النفس اللوّامة
النفس الملهمة
النفس المطمئنة
المجاهدة
الدسائس
الشاذلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul types are separate, fixed categories rather than progressive stages of spiritual development.
Correction: The passage shows a progression: through struggle (mujahada), the soul moves from commanding to blaming to inspired to tranquil. Each stage builds on the previous.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse is cited to support the existence of the tranquil soul (al-nafs al-mutma'innah)?
A) 'Indeed the soul is constantly commanding evil'
B) 'And I swear by the blaming soul'
C) 'Then He inspired it with its wickedness and piety'
D) 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, pleased and pleasing'

Key Takeaway
The soul's spiritual journey is a progressive purification from commanding evil to complete tranquility, each stage marked by distinct Quranic verses and behavioral signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught your own soul tricking you into doing something that looks good (like extra worship or charity) but is really a way to avoid a harder spiritual struggle? What was that struggle you avoided?
?
The blaming soul sees its faults constantly. When you reflect on your day, do you genuinely blame yourself for your sins and shortcomings, or do you quickly make excuses and move on? What would it take for you to truly face one specific fault without despair?
?
The tranquil soul is described as being adorned with God's attributes like mercy, kindness, and generosity. Which of these attributes do you find hardest to embody in your daily interactions? What is one concrete action you can take tomorrow to practice that attribute toward someone you find difficult?

The Inspired Soul (Nafs Mulhama)
Defines the inspired soul and its sign with a warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the inspired soul (nafs mulhama), its sign of recognizing hidden deceits, and the necessity of relying on a shaykh in this hazardous station.

Core Idea
The inspired soul knows its own hidden deceits but cannot escape them without complete reliance on the shaykh.

This lesson explores the third stage of the soul's journey. After struggle and illumination, the soul becomes aware of its own subtle hypocrisies. But this awareness alone is not enough—the passage warns that this station is extremely perilous, and safety lies only in total dependence on a qualified spiritual guide.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the definition and the sign of the inspired soul.
Notice the Quranic reference (Q. 91:8) for the name.
2
Identify the sign and its components
The sign is recognizing subtle deceits. List them: hypocrisy, self-admiration, and others. Understand why these are called 'hidden'.
3
Understand the danger of this station
The text says this station is 'hazardous' and 'usually no one escapes it except by completely relying on his shaykh.' Reflect on why a guide is essential.
The soul is in a state of annihilation (fana') from all besides God, which can be disorienting.
4
Recognize the role of the shaykh
The shaykh provides external support and prevents the seeker from being overwhelmed by the subtle ego traps that the soul now perceives.
This dependence is a recurring theme in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنواع النفوس
- فإذا أخذ في المجاهدة والكَدِّ، حتّى مالت إلى عالم القُدس واستنارت بحيث ألهمت فجورها وتقواها، سُمِّيت ملهمة، وهي الثالثة، وعلامتها أن يعرف صاحبها دسائسها الخفيَّة الدَّقيقة؛ من الرّياء والعجب وغير ذلك.
- فإذا لزم المجاهدة حتّى زالت عنها الشَّهوات، وتبدلت الصفات المذمومة بالمحمودة، وتخلّقت بأخلاق الله تعالى الجمالية؛ من الرّأفة والرَّحمة واللطف والكرم والوُدِّ سُمِّيت مطمئنة، وهي الرابعة، وهذا المقام هو مبدأ الوصول إلى الله تعالى ولكنَّها لا تخلو من دسائس

:
قوله : ( وعلامتها أن يعرف صاحبها دسائسها الخفيَّة) ومن جملة علامتها : الشَّوق، والهيمان، والسكر، إذ هو في هذا المقام فانٍ عمَّا سوى الله تعالى، ولكنَّ هذا المقام كثير العطب لا ينجو منه عادة إلا باستناده لشيخه بالكلية قوله : ( سميت مطمئنة، وهي الرَّابعة : هذه وما بعدها إلى السَّابعة
مأخوذة من قوله تعالى : يَأَيّها النَّفْسُ الْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ارْجِعِي إِلَى رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةً فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِي وَادْخُلِي جَنَّتِي (٢) .
مَرْضِيَّةً
قوله : ( هو مبدأ الوصول) : أي : ولذا يقولون: هو أول قدم يضعه

خفية جداً ؛ كالشّرك الخفيّ وحبِّ الرِّياسة، إلَّا أنَّها لخفائها ودقتها لا يدركها إلّا أهلها الذين نور الله بصائرهم؛ لأنَّ ظاهرها الصَّلاح والاتصاف بالصفات الحميدة من الكرم والحِلم والتّوكُل والزُّهد والورع والشكر والصبر والتسليم والرضا بالقضاء، مع انکشاف بعض أسرار، وانخراقِ بعض عادات وظهور بعض كرامات، فلربما ظنَّ صاحبها أنَّه الإمام الأعظم، وأنَّ مقامه هو المقام الأفخم، وهذا من جملة الدسائس .
- فإذا أدركته العناية الإلهيَّة، واستند إلى شيخه بالكلِّيَّة، ولازم المجاهدة، حتّى تمكّن من الصفات المحمودة، وانقطع عنه عرق الرياء، وصارت نفسه ذليلة، واستوى عنده المدح والذم ودخلت في مقام الفناء، ورضيت بكلِّ ما يقع في الكون من غير اعتراض أصلاً، الخامسة . سميت راضية وهي
ولكن رؤية الفناء والإخلاص ربَّما أوقع في شيء من الإعجاب، فيرجع به القهقرى، فليستعذ بالله من ذلك مداومة الذكر والالتجاء مع
إلى الله وملاحظة أنَّه لا يتمُّ له الخلاص إلا بمدد الشَّيخ .
- فإذا فنى عن الفناء، وخلص من رؤية الإخلاص، تجلّى عليها بالرّضا، وعفا عن كل ما مضى وتبدلت سيئاتها حسنات، وانفتح لها أبواب الأذواق والتّجلّيات، فصارت غريقة في بحار التَّوحيد، وآنستها
المريد في الطريق، وقبله يسمى : مريداً .
قوله : ( في بحار التَّوحيد من إضافة المشبَّه به للمشبَّه، وكذا قوله :
Types of souls. If it (the soul) engages in struggle and exertion until it inclines toward the world of holiness and becomes illuminated so that it is inspired with its wickedness and piety, it is called the inspired soul (nafs mulhama), and it is the third. Its sign is that its possessor knows its subtle hidden deceits: from hypocrisy, self-admiration, and other things. If it persists in struggle until desires leave it, and blameworthy qualities are replaced with praiseworthy ones, and it becomes characterized by the beautiful attributes of God Almighty: compassion, mercy, kindness, generosity, and love, it is called the tranquil soul (nafs mutma'inna), and it is the fourth. This station is the beginning of attaining God Almighty, but it is not free from deceits. And his saying: ('it is called inspired, and it is the third'): meaning it is taken from His statement: (He inspired it with its wickedness and its piety) (1). His saying: ('and its sign is that its possessor knows its hidden deceits') – among its signs are longing, ecstasy, and intoxication, for in this station he is annihilated from all besides God. But this station is hazardous; usually no one escapes it except by completely relying on his shaykh. His saying: ('it is called tranquil, and it is the fourth') – this and what follows up to the seventh are taken from His statement: O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, well-pleased and pleasing, enter among My servants and enter My garden (2). His saying: ('it is the beginning of attainment') – meaning that is why they say: it is the first step that the seeker places. Very hidden, like hidden polytheism and love of leadership, except that due to their hiddenness and subtlety, only those whose insights God has illuminated perceive them; because their outward appearance is righteousness and being characterized with praiseworthy attributes like generosity, forbearance, trust, asceticism, piety, gratitude, patience, submission, and contentment with divine decree, along with the unveiling of some secrets, the breaking of some habits, and the appearance of some miracles (karamat). So perhaps its possessor may think he is the greatest Imam and that his station is the most magnificent station, and this is among the deceits. If divine care reaches him, and he completely relies on his shaykh, and persists in struggle until he becomes established in praiseworthy attributes, and the vein of hypocrisy is cut off, his soul becomes humble, praise and blame become equal to him, he enters the station of annihilation (fana'), and he is content with whatever occurs in existence with no objection at all – (this is) the fifth. It is called the content soul (nafs radiyya), and it is - but the vision of annihilation and sincerity may possibly cause some self-admiration, so he regresses. So he should seek refuge with God from that through constant remembrance and resorting to God, and observing that his deliverance is not completed except through the support of the shaykh. If he becomes annihilated from annihilation and freed from seeing sincerity, contentment manifests upon him, and He pardons all that has passed, and his sins are turned into good deeds, and the doors of spiritual tastes and manifestations open for him, and he becomes drowned in the oceans of divine unity (tawhid), and he becomes familiar with the seeker on the path, and before that he is called a seeker (murid). His saying: ('in the oceans of divine unity') – from the addition of the simile to the simile, and likewise his saying:
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of three stages of the soul: the inspired soul (nafs mulhama), the tranquil soul (nafs mutma'inna), and the content soul (nafs radiyya). The author describes each stage's characteristics, signs, and hidden dangers. The passage begins by defining the third stage: the soul that through struggle in the spiritual path becomes illuminated and is inspired with its own vices and virtues. Its sign is that the person recognizes its subtle deceptions like hypocrisy and self-admiration. Then the author defines the fourth stage: the soul that persists in struggle until desires vanish, blameworthy traits are replaced with praiseworthy ones, and it is adorned with God's attributes. This station is the beginning of reaching God, but it contains hidden deceptions. The author then interjects commentary explaining that the names are derived from Quranic verses (Q. 91:8 and Q. 89:27-30). He also explains the signs of the third stage and warns that this stage is perilous, requiring reliance on a shaykh. For the fourth stage, he notes that it and the subsequent stages up to the seventh are taken from the Quranic verse about the tranquil soul. The author then elaborates on the hidden deceptions of the fourth stage: they are very subtle, like hidden polytheism and love of leadership; only those with divinely illuminated insight can perceive them because outwardly the person appears righteous with praiseworthy qualities and may even experience miraculous events. This can lead the person to think they are the greatest imam, which is itself a deception. The passage then moves to the fifth stage: when divine care reaches the person, they rely entirely on their shaykh, persist in struggle, become firm in praiseworthy attributes, break hypocrisy, become humble, equal in praise and blame, enter the state of annihilation (fana'), and are completely content with God's decree. This soul is called the content soul (radiyya). However, even this stage has a danger: seeing one's own annihilation and sincerity can cause self-admiration, leading to regression. The remedy is constant remembrance and reliance on God and the shaykh. Finally, if the person becomes annihilated from even the awareness of annihilation and frees themselves from seeing their own sincerity, then divine contentment manifests, sins are turned into good deeds, and they become immersed in the oceans of tawhid. At this point they are called a seeker (murid) who is familiar with the path. The passage ends with a grammatical commentary on the phrase 'oceans of tawhid.' Throughout, the author emphasizes that each stage has subtle hidden defects and stresses the necessity of a shaykh for guidance.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that recognizing one's faults automatically protects from them.
Correction: The passage warns that even with awareness, this station is dangerous and requires a shaykh; awareness alone is insufficient.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the sign of the inspired soul (nafs mulhama)?
A) It becomes completely free from all desires.
B) Its possessor knows its subtle hidden deceits like hypocrisy and self-admiration.
C) Its possessor experiences miraculous karamat.
D) Its possessor becomes equal in praise and blame.

Key Takeaway
The inspired soul marks a critical milestone of self-awareness, but it must be coupled with complete submission to a spiritual guide to avoid peril.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have recognized some of your own hidden spiritual diseases. But are you still secretly proud of your self-awareness, relying on your own insight rather than submitting to a guide who can see what you cannot? What would it cost you to truly surrender your self-reliance today?
?
The inspired soul is annihilated from everything except God—yet this very state can lead to imbalance. When you experience moments of spiritual elevation, do you immediately seek the counsel of a shaykh, or do you trust your own intoxication? Your safety depends on the answer.
?
You claim to know your faults, but do you still defend them when a guide points them out? The sign of the inspired soul is not just recognizing deceits—it is the humility to accept that your own awareness is insufficient. Will you commit today to finding a shaykh and obeying him without reservation?
